Salah — Prayer

Order of Rows in Congregational Prayer
Ruling on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order of rows in congregational prayer and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The order of rows between men and women is fard; between men and boys is sunnah.

The arrangement of worshippers in congregational prayer is not arbitrary. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific order based on prophetic practice. This lesson unpacks the ruling for each group—men, boys, hermaphrodites, and women—and explains why the obligation level differs between the male-female and male-boy ordering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the groups and their order
List the four categories in the prescribed sequence: men, boys, hermaphrodites, women. Note that the text treats hermaphrodites as a distinct category placed before women.
The sequence is based on degrees of certainty of masculinity and proximity to the imam.
2
Determine the hukm level for each ordering
Distinguish between the order of men and women (fard) and the order of men and boys (sunnah). The text explicitly states that the latter is sunnah, not fard.
This distinction has practical consequences: if a woman stands in the same row as men, the man's prayer is invalid if he intended to lead her.
3
Locate the dalil for each hukm
For men–women order: the hadith 'أخروهن' (Delay them). For men–boys order: the hadith 'ليليني منكم أولوا الأحلام والنهى' (Let those with dreams and intellect be near me).
Both are ahad hadith, but the text argues this suffices for establishing rules of congregational prayer.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'أخروهن' is a command; in Hanafi usul, commands indicate obligation (wujub). The other hadith implies a recommendation, not an obligation.
The commentator addresses the objection that ahad hadith cannot establish obligation by pointing out that the very obligation of congregational prayer itself is from ahad hadith.
5
Note the status of hermaphrodites
Hermaphrodites (khuntha mushkila) have ambiguous gender, so they are placed after boys (where masculinity is certain) and before women (where masculinity is absent).
This placement is based on probability and preserves the dignity of women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويَصُفُ الرِّجال ، ثم الصبيان ، ثم الخناثى ثم النِّساء.
[٢] قوله : ثم الصبيان ؛ وذلك لأنَّ الرجال أحق بالتقديم، وقرب الإمام يدل عليه حديث: «ليليني منكم أولوا الأحلام والنهى ) ، والأحلام جمع حلم بالضم، وهو البلوغ، والنهى بالضم جمع نهية بمعنى : العقل. والنساء أحق بالتأخير الحديث: «أخروهن من حديث أخرهن الله» (۳) كما مر والصبيان في المرتبة الوسطى، فيكونون بينهما، وقد روى أحمد عن أبي مالك الأشعري الله أنه قال: ألا أريكم صلاة رسول الله، فصلى بالناس وصف الرجال، ثم الولدان، ثم النِّساء»(4).
ثُمَّ الخَناثى ثُمَّ النِّساء : الخناثا بالفتح : جَمْعُ الخُنثى كالحبالى جمع ) الحبلى. (فإن حاذته في صلاة مشتركة تحريمة وأداء ، فَسَدَتْ صلاته إن نَوَى إمامتها ، وإلا صلاتها) وثم الخناثي، والمراد بالخناثى المشكلة : الذين لم يظهر كونهم من الرجال أو النساء، كمن معه علامة الذكور والإناث كليهما ، أو ليس معه شيء بينهما، فلما كانت الرجولية فيهم محتملة ناسب تقديمهم على النساء، ولما كانت الرجولية في الصبيان متيقنة ناسب اتصالهم بالرجال، وتقديمهم على الخناثي.
[١] قوله : ثم النساء ؛ الترتيب بين الرجال والصبيان سُنَّة لا فرض ، وهو الصحيح، أما : بينهم وبين النساء ففرض عندنا. كذا في «الغُنية»)، والأصل فيه حديث : «أخروهن»، فإنّه أمر ويقتضي الافتراض على الإطلاق. فإن قلت : كيف تثبت الفرضية بأخبار الآحاد. قلت : لأن ثبوت أصل الجماعة أيضاً بها، فيصح إثبات متعلقاتها بها. كذا حققه ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير).
He arranges men, then boys, then hermaphrodites, then women. [2] His statement: 'then boys' — because men are more deserving of being forward, and proximity to the imam is indicated by the hadith: 'Let those among you who are possessors of dreams and intellect be next to me' — 'ahlam' is plural of 'hilm' meaning puberty, and 'niha' is plural of 'nihya' meaning intellect. Women are more deserving of being behind due to the hadith: 'Delay them as Allah has delayed them.' Boys are in the middle rank, so they are between them. Ahmad narrated from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari that he said: 'Shall I show you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah?' Then he prayed with the people and arranged the men, then the boys, then the women. Then hermaphrodites, then women: 'khanatha' (with fatha) is plural of 'khuntha' like 'habala' plural of 'hubla' (pregnant). ('If she aligns with him in a shared prayer in both tahrima and performance, then his prayer is invalid if he intended her imamate, otherwise her prayer is invalid.) 'Then the hermaphrodites' — the intended meaning of 'khanatha' is the ambiguous ones who have not become apparent whether they are men or women, like one who has both male and female signs, or has nothing clearly distinguishing them. Since their manhood is probable, it is appropriate to place them before women, and since the manhood of boys is certain, it is appropriate to connect them to men and put them before hermaphrodites. [1] His statement: 'then women' — the order between men and boys is sunnah, not fard, and this is sound. As for the order between men and women, it is fard in our school. Thus in al-Ghunya. The basis is the hadith: 'Delay them,' for it is a command and commands imply obligation absolutely. If you say: How is obligation established by ahad hadith? I say: Because the establishment of the congregational prayer itself is also by ahad hadith, so it is valid to establish its related rulings by them. This is verified by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage explains the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. Men are placed in the front rows, then boys, then hermaphrodites (ambiguous gender), then women at the back. The evidence for men first is the hadith 'Let those with dreams and intellect be near me,' indicating that adult males (possessing reason and maturity) deserve closeness to the imam. Boys are placed behind men because they are less than men in status but more than women. Hermaphrodites (khuntha) are placed before women because their gender is ambiguous, so they are treated with some precedence over women but after boys. The order between men and women is considered obligatory (fard) in the Hanafi school, based on the command 'Delay them' in the hadith. However, the order between men and boys is only sunnah. The commentator also addresses a potential objection: how can an ahad hadith establish an obligation? The answer is that the original obligation of congregational prayer itself is established by ahad hadith, so its details can also be established by such reports.

Key Terms
أحلام (ahlam): Plural of hilm (حلم), meaning puberty/maturity.
نهى (nuha): Plural of nuhyah, meaning intellect.
الخناثى (al-khanatha): Hermaphrodites, ambiguous gender individuals who have both male and female traits or no clear traits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling regarding the order of rows between men and women in congregational prayer?
A) It is sunnah, not obligatory.
B) It is fard (obligatory).
C) It is merely recommended.
D) It is disliked.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, men and women must not stand in the same row; the order is fard and violating it can invalidate the imam's prayer if he intended to lead the woman.

Woman Aligning with Imam Invalidates Prayer: Hanafi vs. Majority
Ruling on horizontal alignment of a woman with the imam in shared prayer with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman aligning with the imam during prayer, explain the evidence from the hadith and istihsan, and compare it with the majority position.

Core Idea
A woman aligning horizontally with the imam invalidates the prayer depending on the imam's intention.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school holds that if a woman stands beside the imam during congregational prayer, the prayer becomes invalid, while the three other imams and the majority consider it valid. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith 'أخروهن' (delay them) and uses istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas. Understanding this ruling is essential for proper congregational prayer arrangement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and Hanafi ruling
The scenario: a woman aligns horizontally with the imam in a shared prayer (both in the opening takbir and performance). The ruling: the prayer is invalid. If the imam intended to lead her, his prayer is invalid; otherwise, her prayer is invalid.
2
Recognize the disagreement
The three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) and the majority hold that the prayer remains valid. They base this on qiyas: alignment does not affect the essence of prayer.
The majority view is the apparent qiyas.
3
Understand the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi school uses istihsan based on the hadith 'أخروهن' (delay them). They interpret this imperative as an obligation on men to keep women behind them. Violation of this obligation invalidates the man's prayer.
The command is addressed to men, not women.
4
Analyze the reasoning
The man's failure to delay the woman is a violation of a compulsory standing condition, thus invalidating his prayer. The woman is also commanded to stay behind, but her obligation is implicit; if she deliberately aligns, her prayer may be invalid.
The text distinguishes between intentional and unintentional actions.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis must ensure women stand behind men. If a woman stands beside the imam, the prayer may need to be repeated depending on intention.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن حاذته في صلاة مشتركة تحريمة وأداء ، فَسَدَتْ صلاته إن نَوَى إمامتها ، وإلا صلاتها.
[١] قوله : فسدت صلاته ; خالفنا فيه الأئمة الثلاثة والجمهور، فقالوا بعـدم الفساد وهو القياس إلا أن أئمتنا استحسنوا بالحديث، وهو: «أخـروهـن...» الخ، ووجهوه بأنه يدلّ على افتراض التأخير، والمخاطب به هو الرجل، فيكون ترك التأخير منه مفسداً بترك فرض المقام، فيفسد صلاته لا صلاتها. وإن كانت مأمورة بالتأخر ،ضمناً، ويحرم عليها تركه فرقاً بين القصدي
If she aligns with him in a shared prayer in both tahrima and performance, then his prayer is invalid if he intended her imamate, otherwise her prayer is invalid. [1] His statement: 'His prayer is invalid' — the three imams and the majority disagreed with us, saying there is no invalidation, and that is qiyas. However, our imams used istihsan based on the hadith: 'Delay them...' and they reasoned it indicates the obligation of delay, and the addressee is the man, so his failure to delay invalidates his prayer due to leaving an obligatory standing, not her prayer. Although she is also commanded to be behind, implicitly, and it is prohibited for her to leave it, distinguishing between the intentional and unintentional.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute about the effect of a woman standing beside the imam in a shared prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that if a woman aligns horizontally with the imam during the prayer (both in the opening tahrimah and the actual performance), then the prayer becomes invalid. If the man (imam) intended to lead her, his prayer is invalid; otherwise, her prayer is invalid. The three other imams (presumably Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) and the majority hold that the prayer remains valid, which is the apparent qiyas. The Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) based on the hadith 'Delay them' (أخروهن). They argue that the command to delay is addressed to men, meaning it is obligatory for men to ensure women are behind them. By allowing a woman to align with him, the man violates this obligation, thus his prayer is invalid. The woman, however, is also commanded to stay behind, but her obligation is implicit; if she deliberately aligns, her prayer may be invalid as well. The text distinguishes between intentional and unintentional acts.

Key Terms
حاذته (hadhatuhu): To be parallel or aligned horizontally with someone (here, the woman aligning with the imam).
استحسن (istahsana): To prefer a ruling based on istihsan (juristic preference) over qiyas, due to a stronger evidence or public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a woman aligns horizontally with the imam during a congregational prayer and the imam intended to lead her?
A) Both prayers are valid.
B) Only the woman's prayer is invalid.
C) The imam's prayer is invalid.
D) Both prayers are invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a woman aligning with the imam invalidates the prayer of the one whose intention caused the alignment, based on the hadith and istihsan.

Invalidation of Prayer by Alignment with Women and Khuntha
Ruling on invalidity due to alignment with women/khuntha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on alignment with women/khuntha in congregational prayer, identify the conditions for invalidity, and explain the istihsan-based proof against the opposing schools' qiyas.

Core Idea
If a woman aligns with a man in shared prayer, his prayer invalidates if he intended to lead her, otherwise hers invalidates.

The Hanafi school holds a unique position on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer. While other schools consider the order of men and women merely recommended, the Hanafis treat it as obligatory, such that violation can invalidate the prayer. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, the proof from the hadith 'Akhkhiruhunna', and the inter-madhhab dispute with the three Imams. Understanding this ruling illuminates the Hanafi use of istihsan over qiyas and the epistemological weight given to established practice and consensus.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling and row order
Identify the required order: men, then boys, then khuntha (ambiguous gender), then women. Note that alignment (muhadhat) by a woman or khuntha can invalidate the prayer of either the man (if he intended to lead) or the woman (if he did not).
The ruling distinguishes based on the man's intention to lead.
2
Identify the proof and its epistemological basis
Locate the primary proof: the hadith 'Akhkhiruhunna' (Delay them). Understand that Hanafis treat this command as obligatory (fard) even though it is an ahad hadith. They argue that since congregational prayer itself is established by ahad reports, its details similarly can be.
This addresses the objection that ahad reports cannot establish obligation.
3
Trace the istihsan reasoning
See how Hanafis depart from qiyas (which would keep the prayer valid) and use istihsan based on the hadith. They interpret the command as addressed to the man, so his violation invalidates his prayer, analogous to a follower stepping ahead of the imam.
The analogy with imam and follower clarifies why only one party's prayer is invalidated.
4
List the five conditions for invalidity
Extract from the text the conditions: (1) woman is adult or desirable girl, (2) she understands the prayer, (3) alignment lasts a pillar or she performs a pillar (intra-Hanafi difference), (4) prayer has bowing and prostration, (5) prayer is shared in takbirat al-ihram.
These conditions restrict the application, so not every alignment invalidates.
5
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Compare the Hanafi position (invalidates) with that of the three Imams and majority (valid). The opposing qiyas is that one person's prayer is not invalidated by another's position. Hanafis counter with istihsan and consensus on delaying women.
The dispute is practical: validity vs. invalidity of the prayer.

Source Text

ثُمَّ الخناثى ، ثُمَّ النِّساء : الخناثا بالفتح : جَمْعُ الخُنثى كالحبالى جمع ) الحبلى. (فإن حاذته في صلاة مشتركة تحريمة وأداء ، فَسَدَتْ صلاته إن نَوَى إمامتها ، وإلا صلاتها) وثم الخناثي، والمراد بالخناثى المشكلة : الذين لم يظهر كونهم من الرجال أو النساء، كمن معه علامة الذكور والإناث كليهما ، أو ليس معه شيء بينهما، فلما كانت الرجولية فيهم محتملة ناسب تقديمهم على النساء، ولما كانت الرجولية في الصبيان متيقنة ناسب اتصالهم بالرجال، وتقديمهم على الخناثي.
[١] قوله : ثم النساء ؛ الترتيب بين الرجال والصبيان سُنَّة لا فرض ، وهو الصحيح، أما : بينهم وبين النساء ففرض عندنا. كذا في «الغُنية»)، والأصل فيه حديث : «أخروهن»، فإنّه أمر ويقتضي الافتراض على الإطلاق. فإن قلت : كيف تثبت الفرضية بأخبار الآحاد. قلت : لأن ثبوت أصل الجماعة أيضاً بها، فيصح إثبات متعلقاتها بها. كذا حققه ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير).

وعن أبي مالك الأشعري : أن النبي ل الله صلى فأقام الرجال يلونه خلف ذلك، وأقام النساء خلف ذلك» في المعجم الكبير (۳) : ۲۹۱)، وقال : «خير صفوف الرجال أولها وشرها آخرها، وخير صفوف النساء آخرها وشرها أولها» في «صحیح مسلم (٢ : ٤٣٥).
أي إن صلت"
والضمـني، وكان وزانه معها في لزوم تقدّمه وتأخرها ، وزان المأموم مع الإمام في لزوم تأخره، وتقام الإمام، فكما أنّ المأموم لا يجوز له التقدّم وتفسد صلاته، والإمام لا يجوز له التأخر ولكن لا تفسد صلاته كذلك.
وهذا كله مبني على ثبوت الحديث المذكور بسند معتبر مرفوعاً إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم يثبت ذلك، وإنّما روي موقوفا علی ابن مسعود ، وكذا حققه في «فتح » و«الغنية»، وفي المقام أبحاث موضع بسطها «السعاية».
قوله : أي إن صلت.... الخ ؛ ذكر في «الهداية»(۳) و«الغُنية» وغيرهما : «أن للفساد بالمحاذاة عندنا شروطاً ، وقد أشار الشارح والمصنف إلى أكثرها :
الأول : كون المرأة بالغة أو صبية مشتهاة.
الثاني : كونها تعقل الصلاة.
الثالث : أن تكون المحاذاة قدر ركن عند محمد الله ، وأداء الركن معها عند أبي يوسف .
الرابع : أن تكون الصلاة ذات ركوع وسجود، فلا تفسد المحاذاة في صلاة الجنازة، وسجدة التلاوة
الخامس : كون الصلاة مشتركة تحريمية.
(يخطر ببالي أنه لا يتوقف هذا على ثبوت الحديث مرفوعاً، فقد جاء الأمر من الله بل بالعفة والتنزه عن مخالطة النساء والابتعاد عن كلِّ ما فيه إيثارة للشهوة ، واشتهر تأخير رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم للنساء في الصلاة تطبيقاً لهذه الأسس في علاقة الرجل بالمرأة، وصار على ذلك الإجماع في تأخير النساء، وممن نقله ابن مسعود له في قوله : «أخـروهن»، ولم يخالفه أحـد مـن الصحابة ، فتكون المسألة من الإجماعات المشهورة، وقد أفادت عندنا بطلان صلاة الرجل لعدم قيامه بذلك، وأما عدم بطلانها عند غيرنا فليس لعدم ثبوت هذا الإجماع، وإنما هو راجع للاستدلال به كما هو الحال في ثبوت القرآن والاختلاف في إفادته للأحكام والله أعلم، وعلمه أحكم.
Then the khunatha (hermaphrodites), then the women. If she aligns with him in a prayer shared in takbirat al-ihram and performance, his prayer becomes invalid if he intended to lead her, otherwise her prayer becomes invalid. Then the khunatha, then the women: al-khanatha (with fatha) is plural of khuntha like habala is plural of hubla. (If she aligns with him in a prayer shared in takbirat al-ihram and performance, his prayer becomes invalid if he intended to lead her, otherwise her prayer becomes invalid.) And then the khunatha, and by khunatha is meant the ambiguous ones: those whose status as male or female is not apparent, such as one who has both male and female signs, or has no clear sign of either. Since masculinity in them is probable, it is appropriate to place them before women; and since masculinity in boys is certain, it is appropriate to connect them with men and place them before khunatha.
[1] His statement: 'then the women'; the order between men and boys is sunnah, not obligatory, and that is correct. As for between them and women, it is obligatory according to us. Thus in al-Ghunya, and the basis for it is the hadith: 'Delay them (women),' for it is a command and necessitates obligation absolutely. If you say: How is obligation established by ahad reports? I say: Because the establishment of the origin of congregational prayer is also by them, so it is valid to establish its related matters by them. Thus verified by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.
[2] His statement: 'his prayer became invalid'; the three Imams and the majority differed with us on this, saying there is no invalidity, and that is the analogy. However, our Imams used istihsan based on the hadith: 'Delay them...' etc., and they explained it by saying it indicates the obligation of delay, and the addressee is the man, so his leaving the delay invalidates his prayer due to leaving an obligatory place, so his prayer is invalidated, not hers. Even though she is commanded to delay implicitly, and it is prohibited for her to leave it, distinguishing between intentional and implicit. And from Abu Malik al-Ash'ari that the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) prayed and made the men stand behind him, and made the women stand behind that... in al-Mu'jam al-Kabir (3:291), and he said: 'The best of men's rows is the first and the worst is the last; the best of women's rows is the last and the worst is the first' in Sahih Muslim (2:435).
Meaning, if she prays... and the implicit, and his position with her regarding the necessity of his precedence and her delay is like the position of the follower with the imam regarding the necessity of his delay and the imam's precedence. Just as the follower may not go ahead and his prayer is invalidated, and the imam may not delay but his prayer is not invalidated, similarly.
All of this is based on the establishment of the aforementioned hadith with a reliable chain raised to the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam), but that is not established; rather it is reported as stopped (mawquf) on Ibn Mas'ud. Thus verified in Fath and al-Ghunya, and there are investigations in this place that are elaborated in al-Si'aya.
His statement: 'meaning if she prayed...' etc.; it is mentioned in al-Hidaya and al-Ghunya and others: 'Invalidity due to alignment according to us has conditions, and the commentator and author have indicated most of them:
First: The woman is an adult or a desirable girl.
Second: She understands the prayer.
Third: The alignment is for the duration of a pillar according to Muhammad (rahimahullah), or performance of a pillar with her according to Abu Yusuf.
Fourth: The prayer involves bowing and prostration, so alignment does not invalidate in funeral prayer or prostration of recitation.
Fifth: The prayer is shared in takbirat al-ihram.'
(It occurs to me that this does not depend on establishing the hadith as raised; rather the command came from Allah regarding chastity and abstaining from mixing with women and avoiding everything that arouses desire, and the Prophet's (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) delaying of women in prayer became well-known as an application of these principles in the relationship between men and women, and there was consensus on delaying women. Among those who transmitted it is Ibn Mas'ud in his statement: 'Delay them,' and no Companion opposed him. So the matter is from the well-known consensuses, and it has benefited, according to us, the invalidity of the man's prayer due to his failure to do that. As for its non-invalidity according to others, it is not due to the non-establishment of this consensus, but rather it goes back to using it as evidence, just as is the case with the establishment of the Quran and the difference in its indication of rulings. And Allah knows best, and His knowledge is wisest.)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on the ruling regarding women and khunatha (hermaphrodites) aligning with men in congregational prayer. The passage type is a ruling with proof, including an inter-madhhab dispute.

The text begins by stating the order of rows: first men, then boys, then khunatha (those whose gender is ambiguous), then women. If a woman or khuntha aligns with a man in a prayer that is shared in both takbirat al-ihram (the opening proclamation) and the actual performance (i.e., they start together and pray together), then:
- If the man intended to lead her (as imam), his prayer becomes invalid.
- If he did not intend to lead her, her prayer becomes invalid.

The commentary explains that 'khunatha' are those with unclear gender, either having both or no signs. Boys precede khunatha because their masculinity is certain.

Then the text addresses two points. First, the order between men and boys is sunnah (not obligatory), but between men and women it is obligatory (fard) according to the Hanafi school. This is based on the hadith 'Akhkhiruhunna' (Delay them), which is a command indicating obligation. Some object that ahad hadith cannot establish obligation, but the Hanafi response is that the obligation of congregational prayer itself is established by ahad reports, so its details can be as well.

Second, the text notes that the three other Imams (al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) and the majority disagree with the Hanafi ruling of invalidity. They say the prayer remains valid, which is the analogical reasoning (qiyas). However, the Hanafis use istihsan (juristic preference) based on the hadith 'Akhkhiruhunna'. The reasoning: the hadith commands delay, and the addressee is the man. If he fails to delay women (by allowing them to align with him), he has violated an obligation, thus his prayer is invalidated. The woman is commanded to be behind implicitly, but her violation does not invalidate her prayer if she is not the one addressed directly. The commentary draws an analogy with the imam and follower: the follower cannot go ahead (invalidates his prayer), but if the imam delays, his prayer is not invalidated.

However, the text acknowledges that this ruling depends on the authenticity of the hadith as marfu' (raised to the Prophet). In fact, it is reported as mawquf (stopped) on Ibn Mas'ud. Nevertheless, the author suggests that even without that, there is established practice and consensus (ijma') on delaying women, so the ruling stands.

Finally, the text lists five conditions for the invalidity:
1. The woman is an adult or a desirable girl (sabiyyah mushtahat).
2. She understands the prayer (i.e., is sane and knows what she is doing).
3. The alignment lasts for the duration of a pillar (rukn) according to Imam Muhammad, or the performance of a pillar with her according to Imam Abu Yusuf.
4. The prayer involves bowing and prostration (so not funeral prayer or prostration of recitation).
5. The prayer is shared in takbirat al-ihram (i.e., they start at the same time).

In summary, the Hanafi school holds that under these conditions, the man's or woman's prayer may be invalidated due to alignment, based on istihsan from the hadith and established practice.

Key Terms
خنثى (ج. خناثى) (khuntha (pl. khunatha)): A person of ambiguous gender, having both or no clear signs of male or female. In the context of prayer rows, they are placed after boys and before women.
محاذاة (muhadhat): Alignment (shoulder-to-shoulder) of a woman or khuntha with a man in the same row of congregational prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from the literal analogy (qiyas) in favor of a stronger evidence (here, the hadith and established practice).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the conditions listed in the passage, in which of the following prayers would alignment of a woman with a man potentially invalidate the prayer?
A) Funeral prayer (salat al-janazah)
B) Prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah)
C) Fajr prayer (with bowing and prostration)
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that under five specific conditions, alignment of a woman with a man in congregational prayer invalidates the prayer of one of them, based on istihsan from the command 'Delay them' and established practice.

Conditions for Invalidation of Prayer Due to a Woman's Alignment (Muhadhat)
Enumeration and explanation of ten conditions for fasad due to muhadhat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten conditions for invalidation (fasād) of a man's prayer due to a woman's alignment and explain the Hanafi proof for this ruling.

Core Idea
A man's prayer is invalidated only when all ten conditions of muhādhat are met — a uniquely Hanafi position.

This passage from ʿUmdat al-Riʿāyah enumerates the conditions under which a woman's alignment next to a man during prayer invalidates his prayer according to the Hanafi school. It also discusses the evidentiary basis (the narration of Ibn Masʿūd and the consensus of the Companions) and notes intra-madhhab differences between Imām Muḥammad and Abū Yūsuf regarding the required duration. Understanding these conditions is essential to applying the ruling correctly and avoiding the misconception that any proximity invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Recognize that the passage discusses the invalidation (fasād) of a man's prayer when a woman aligns next to him. Note that this is a Hanafi-specific ruling derived from a mawqūf narration of Ibn Masʿūd and consensus.
2
Enumerate the ten conditions
List the ten conditions given in the text: woman is adult or desirable minor, understands prayer, alignment lasts a rukn (or performs with her), prayer has rukūʿ and sujūd, shared takbīr, shared performance, same place, same direction, no barrier, imam intends to lead women.
Conditions 3 has an intra-madhhab difference between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
3
Analyze the proof structure
The proof is a mawqūf narration from Ibn Masʿūd ('Akhkhirūhunna') backed by the general practice of the Prophet and consensus. The commentator argues the ruling holds even if the hadith is not marfūʿ due to the consensus.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad requires alignment for the duration of one rukn (pillar), while Abu Yusuf requires that the pillar be performed during alignment. Both views are accepted in the school.
5
Apply the scope: how many men are affected?
One woman invalidates the prayer of up to three men (left, right, behind). Two women invalidate up to four. This limitation is derived from the text.

Two women invalidate the prayer of four.' His saying: 'like the followers': what is meant is the one who catches the prayer (mudrik), for 'muqtadi' means one who follows an imam, also called 'mu'tamm'. Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditions for invalidation of prayer when a woman aligns next to a man in congregation. The author first discusses the hadith basis, noting that it is not proven as marfu' but as mawquf on Ibn Mas'ud. However, he argues that the ruling does not depend solely on that hadith, since the general command of chastity and the established practice of the Prophet ﷺ and consensus of the Companions (citing Ibn Mas'ud's statement 'akhkhiruhunna' – delay them) supports the invalidation for the man who fails to maintain proper distance. The passage then enumerates ten conditions for fasad in the Hanafi school: (1) the woman is adult or a desirable minor; (2) she understands prayer; (3) the alignment lasts for the duration of one pillar (Muhammad) or includes performance of the pillar (Abu Yusuf); (4) the prayer involves bowing and prostration (thus excluding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation); (5) the prayer is shared in the opening takbir (both started with the same imam); (6) the prayer is shared in performance (both are following the same imam); (7) unity of place (e.g., both on the same level); (8) unity of direction (facing the same qiblah); (9) no barrier between them; (10) the imam intends to lead women. The author also clarifies that if the imam does not intend to lead the woman, then her prayer is invalidated, not his. Additionally, if a woman aligns next to a man, it invalidates the prayer of up to three men (one on each side and one behind) but no more; two women invalidate up to four men. The passage defines terms like mudrik (one who catches the full prayer) and lahiq (one who misses part). The overall hukm is that the man's prayer becomes fasid (invalid) under these conditions, which is a specific ruling within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
محاذاة (muhādhat): Alignment of a woman next to a man during prayer, which can invalidate the prayer under specific conditions.
صلاة مشتركة تحريمية (ṣalāt mushtarakah taḥrīmiyyah): Prayer that is shared in the opening takbir, meaning both the man and woman are following the same imam from the start.
شركة في الأداء (shirkah fī al-adā'): Sharing in performance of the prayer, i.e., both are following the same imam during the actions of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a man's prayer is invalidated due to a woman's alignment only when all ten conditions are simultaneously present.

Ruling on Woman Praying Beside Man and Types of Followers in Congregation
Conditions for invalidity and follower classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's adjacency invalidates prayer, and distinguish between the three types of followers (mudrik, lahiq, masbuq) with their respective rulings.

Core Idea
A woman's adjacency invalidates only if she is desirable, no barrier, shared prayer, and imam intends leading women; followers are classified by their completeness with the imam.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a critical fiqh ruling regarding women praying beside men in congregation. It lists the precise conditions for invalidity, emphasizing that not every adjacency causes invalidity. Additionally, the passage clarifies the categories of followers: mudrik (complete), lahiq (misses part due to excuse), and masbuq (joins late). Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the rules of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage addresses the scenario of a woman praying beside a man. The ruling is that the prayer becomes fasid (invalid) under specific conditions. Note that invalidity applies to either the man or the woman depending on the imam's intention.
2
List the conditions for invalidity
Extract the ten conditions mentioned: shared tahrimah, shared ada', unity of place, unity of direction, no barrier, imam's intention to lead women, and that the woman is desirable (mushatah). Also note exceptions: adolescent boy, inside Ka'ba.
The condition 'woman is desirable' excludes mahram and very old women.
3
Note the role of intention
The invalidity depends on whether the imam intended to lead women. If yes, the man's prayer is invalid; if no, the woman's prayer is invalid.
4
Understand the classification of followers
Mudrik completes prayer with imam; lahiq starts with imam but misses some rak'ats due to an excuse (e.g., hadath, sleep); masbuq joins after imam has started. Each has different rulings for recitation and making up missed parts.
The lahiq is considered legally behind the imam even if the imam has finished.
5
Apply to the detailed example
Work through the example of two lahiqs (a man and a woman) who experience hadath, perform wudu, and resume after the imam finishes. The woman aligns with the man, causing the man's prayer to be invalid because she is a desirable woman and the lahiq is still in the ruling of following the imam legally.

وآخر عن خلفها ليس غير؛ فإنّ من فسدت حائلا يصير بينه وبين الذي يليه، والمرأتان صلاة أربعة». قوله : كالمقتديين؛ المراد بهما المدركان، فإنّ المقتدي بمعنى من يقتدي بإمام، ويقال له: المؤتم أيضاً إن صلاها كاملة مع الإمام، يقال له: المدرك، وإن فاتته الركعاتُ كلّها أو بعضها بعد اقتدائه بعذر كغفلة وزحمة ونوم وسبق حدث، يقال له: اللاحق، ويفسر بمن يدرك أوّل صلاة الإمام، ويفوت منه أوسطها أو آخرها، وإن فاته أوّل ... ثم يتابع إمامه إن أدركه... ففي «شرح المنية»: «وحكمه أنه يقضي ما فاته أولا ثم يتابع الإمام إن لم يكن قد فرغ». وفي «البحر» : هو حكمه أنه يبدأ بقضاء ما فاته بالعذر ثم يتابع الإمام إن لم يفرغ وهذا واجب لا شرط، حتى وإما حُكْماً كاللاحقين يعني رجل وامرأة اقتديا برجل فسبقهما حدث فتوضئا وبنيا، وقد فَرَغَ الإمام، فحاذت المرأةُ الرَّجلَ فسدت صلاةُ الرَّجل. فاللاحق وإن لم يكن له إمام حقيقة، فله إمام حكماً، فإنَّه التزم أن يؤدِّي جميع صلاتِه خَلْفَ الإمام، فإذا سبقَهُ الحدث فتوضأ وبنا، يُجْعَل كأَنَّه خَلْفَ الإمام حتَّى يثبت له أحكامُ المقتديين كحرمة القراءة، ونحوها بخلاف المسبوق: وهو الذي أدرك آخر صلاة الإمام، فلم يلتزم أداءَ الكُلِّ خَلْفَ الإمام صلاته معه يقال له: المسبوق. كذا في «الدر المختار» وحواشيه. قوله: فسبقهما؛ أي عرض لهما حدث ناقض للوضوء في أثناء الصلاة، فذهبا للتوضؤ وقد فرغ الإمام عن صلاته، فجاءا فبنيا؛ أي صليا ما بقي من صلاتهما كل واحد منهما على حدة كما هو حكم اللاحق. قوله: فإنه التزم؛ حيث دخل معه مقتدياً من أول صلاته، وقصد أن يؤدي معه كلّها إلا أنه لم يحصل له ذلك؛ لعذر لحقه بدون اختياره. قوله: يجعل؛ بصيغة المجهول؛ أي يجعل شرعاً أنه خلف الإمام، فكان له إماماً حكماً. قوله: حتى...الخ؛ تفريع على كونه خلف الإمام حكماً. قوله: كحرمة القراءة؛ في إطلاق الحرمة مسامحة، فإن قراءة القرآن للمقتدي عند أصحابنا مكروهة لا حرام، لكن لما صرَّحوا أنّ الكراهة تحريمية أطلق عليها الحرمة؛ لقربها منها. قوله: ونحوها؛ أي غيرها من الأحكام الثابتة للمدرك، فلا يأتي بسجدة سهو بما يسهو فيما يؤدّيه، ولا يتغير فرضُهُ بنيّة إقامته في أثناء صلاته إن كان مسافرا، ويخالفه لو عكسه يصح، فلو نام في الثالثة واستيقظ في الرابعة. فإنه يأتي بالثالثة بلا قراءة . فإذا فرغ منها صلى مع الإمام الرابعة، وإن فرغ منها الإمام صلاها وحده بلا قراءة أيضا؛ فلو تابع الإمام ثم قضى الثالثة بعد سلام الإمام صح وأثم. ينظر: رد المحتار (1:595)، وغيره. (1) «الدر المختار و رد المحتار (1:594)، وغيرها.
That if a woman who is desirable prays beside a man such that there is no barrier between them, and the prayer is shared in tahrimah and ada', then the man's prayer is invalid if the imam intended leadership of women, and if he did not intend, the woman's prayer is invalid. And they explained sharing in tahrimah: that both base their opening takbir on the imam's opening takbir. And sharing in ada': that they have an imam in what they perform, either in reality like the followers. Sixth: the prayer being shared in terms of performance. Seventh: unity of place, so if one is on a platform the height of a man and the other on the ground, it does not invalidate. Eighth: unity of direction, so if they differ as if they pray inside the Ka'ba, it does not invalidate. Ninth: absence of barrier between them. Tenth: that the imam intends leadership of women. His statement: 'on the side of a man a woman' – as for an adolescent boy, his alignment does not invalidate, and the saying of invalidity is rejected, as in al-Fath and al-Ghunya. His statement: 'the man's prayer is invalid' – he said in Fath al-Qadeer: 'One woman invalidates the prayer of three: one on her right, another on her left, and another behind her, not more; for whoever's prayer is invalidated becomes a barrier between him and the one next to him, and two women invalidate the prayer of four.' His statement: 'like the followers' – what is meant is the mudrikun, for al-muqtadi means one who follows an imam, and he is also called al-mu'tam if he prays it completely with the imam, he is called al-mudrik; and if all or some rak'ats are missed after his following due to an excuse like inattention, crowding, sleep, or preceding hadath, he is called al-lahiq; and it is interpreted as one who catches the beginning of the imam's prayer and misses its middle or end; and if he misses the beginning... then he follows his imam if he catches him... in Sharh al-Munya: 'His ruling is that he makes up what he missed first then follows the imam if he has not finished.' And in al-Bahr: his ruling is that he begins by making up what he missed due to the excuse then follows the imam if he has not finished, and this is obligatory not a condition, until... And by way of legal ruling, like the two lahiqs: meaning a man and a woman who followed a man, and then hadath preceded them, so they performed wudu and resumed, and the imam had finished, and the woman aligned with the man, so the man's prayer is invalid. The lahiq, even if he does not have an imam in reality, he has a legal imam, for he committed to perform all of his prayer behind the imam; so if hadath preceded him, he performs wudu and resumes, he is considered as if behind the imam so that the rulings of the followers apply to him, like the prohibition of recitation, etc., unlike the masbuq: he is the one who catches the end of the imam's prayer, so he did not commit to perform all behind the imam; his prayer with him is called al-masbuq. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its glosses. His statement: 'hadath preceded them' – meaning an event that invalidates wudu occurred to them during the prayer, so they went to perform wudu while the imam had finished his prayer, so they came and resumed; i.e., they prayed what remained of their prayer each separately as is the ruling of the lahiq. His statement: 'for he committed' – since he entered with him as a follower from the beginning of his prayer and intended to perform all with him, but that did not happen for him due to an excuse that befell him without his choice. His statement: 'he is made' – in the passive voice; i.e., he is made legally as behind the imam, so he has a legal imam. His statement: 'until...etc.' – a branching on his being legally behind the imam. His statement: 'like the prohibition of recitation' – in using 'prohibition' there is tolerance, for recitation of Quran for the follower according to our companions is disliked (makruh) not haram, but since they stated that the dislike is of the prohibitory level, they called it prohibition due to its closeness. His statement: 'and the like' – i.e., other rulings established for the mudrik, such that he does not perform prostrations of forgetfulness for what he forgets in what he performs, and his obligation does not change by his intention of residence during his prayer if he is a traveler, and if the opposite occurs it is valid; if he sleeps in the third and wakes in the fourth, he performs the third without recitation, then when he finishes it, he prays the fourth with the imam; and if the imam finishes it, he prays it alone without recitation also; if he follows the imam and then makes up the third after the imam's salam, it is valid but sinful. See Radd al-Mukhtar (1:595) and others. (1) al-Durr al-Mukhtar wa Radd al-Mukhtar (1:594) and others.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding a woman praying beside a man in congregation. It begins by stating the basic ruling: if a desirable woman (mushatah) prays beside a man with no barrier, and their prayers are shared in both the opening takbir (tahrimah) and performance (ada'), then the man's prayer is invalid if the imam intended to lead women; otherwise, the woman's prayer is invalid. The sharing in takbir means both initiate their prayer based on the imam's takbir, and sharing in performance means they have the same imam. The text then lists conditions for invalidity: the prayer must be shared in performance, unity of place (even if one is on a higher platform), unity of direction (if different, as inside Ka'ba, no invalidity), no barrier, and the imam's intention to lead women. The commentary clarifies that an adolescent boy's adjacency does not cause invalidity, citing Fath al-Qadeer. It also notes that one woman can invalidate the prayers of up to three men: one on her right, left, and behind, and two women invalidate four men. The passage then explains the types of followers: mudrik (one who completes with imam), lahiq (one who misses some rak'ats due to excuse and catches up), and masbuq (one who joins later and does not complete all behind imam). A detailed example is given: a man and woman follow an imam, both have hadath, they perform wudu and resume after imam finishes; if the woman aligns with the man, his prayer is invalid because the lahiq is considered legally behind the imam. The lahiq is treated as still behind the imam legally, so rulings like prohibition of recitation apply. Recitation is actually makruh tahrimi, not haram. Other rulings for the mudrik are mentioned: no sajda sahw for his own forgetfulness, no change of obligation if he intends residence while traveling, etc. The passage relies on Hanafi sources like Fath al-Qadeer, Ghunya, Sharh al-Munya, al-Bahr, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Radd al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
مشتهاة (mushatah): A woman who is likely to attract desire, i.e., not a close relative or aged woman.
اشتراك في التحريمة (ishtirak fi al-tahrimah): Both followers base their opening takbir on the imam's takbir, i.e., they initiate prayer concurrently.
مدرك (mudrik): A person who performs the entire prayer with the imam from beginning to end without missing any part.
لاحق (lahiq): A person who starts with the imam but misses some rak'ats due to an excuse like sleep, inattention, or hadath, and then makes them up.
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregation after the imam has already started, catching only the end of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect if an imam does NOT intend to lead women while a desirable woman prays beside a man with all other conditions met?
A) The man's prayer becomes invalid
B) The woman's prayer becomes invalid
C) Both prayers become invalid
D) Neither prayer is affected

Key Takeaway
A woman's adjacency in congregation invalidates prayer only if she is desirable, all conditions are met, and the imam intends to lead women; otherwise, it is the woman's prayer that is invalid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Lahiq: Legal Definition and Rulings
Defines al-lahiq and establishes his legal status as a virtual follower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-lahiq in Hanafi fiqh and state the rulings that apply to him as a virtual follower.

Core Idea
The lahiq, though physically separated, remains in the legal status of a follower throughout his prayer.

In congregational prayer, a person may be forced to interrupt his prayer due to an unavoidable event, like losing wudu. After returning, how should he resume? The Hanafi school distinguishes between two scenarios: the lahiq (who started with the imam) and the masbuq (who joined late). This lesson defines the lahiq and explains his unique rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lahiq's defining feature
The lahiq started the prayer with the imam from the beginning, intending to follow him completely. An excusable interruption occurs, causing him to leave and return.
The interruption must be due to a valid excuse like loss of wudu.
2
Understand the legal principle
Despite physical separation, the lahiq is considered (hukman) behind the imam because he committed (iltazama) to perform his entire prayer behind the imam.
This is a key point: the intention at the start creates a legal bond that persists even after interruption.
3
Apply the rulings of a follower
Since he is a virtual follower, he must not recite behind the imam (recitation is makruh tanzihi for the follower). He also does not perform sajdah sahw for mistakes in his own remaining prayer, and his obligation (e.g., qasr) does not change by intention during his prayer.
The passage mentions several rulings: 'and the like'.
4
Analyze the scenario of alignment
When two lahiqs (a man and a woman) return and the woman aligns with the man, the man's prayer becomes invalid because they are still partners in performance under the same imam.
This illustrates the virtual partnership.

وإما حُكْماً كاللاحقين يعني رجل وامرأة اقتديا برجل فسبقهما حدث فتوضئا وبنيا، وقد فَرَغَ الإمام ، فحاذت المرأةُ الرَّجلَ فسدت صلاةُ الرَّجل. فاللاحق وإن لم يكن له إمام حقيقة ، فله إمام حكماً، فإنَّه التزم أن يؤدِّي جميع صلاتِه خَلْفَ الإمام ، فإذا سبقَهُ الحدث فتوضأ وبنا، يُجْعَل كأَنَّه خَلْفَ الإمام حتَّى يثبت له أحكامُ المقتديين كحرمة القراءة، ونحوها بخلاف المسبوق : وهو الذي أدرك آخر صلاة الإمام، فلم يلتزم أداءَ الكُلِّ خَلْفَ الإمام . فهو في أداء ما لم يُدْرِكْهُ مع الإمام منفرد حتَّى تَجِبَ عليه القراءة، فالمسبوقان وإن كانا مشتركين في التَّحريمةِ إذ بنيا تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام، فليسا مشتركين أداء، فإن حاذت المرأةُ رجلاً في أداء ما سبق، لم تفسد صلاة الرجل ؛ لعدم الشركة في الأداء.

٣. ومنها : أنه لو قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به وعلى الإمام سجدتا سهو، ولو كان قبل اقتدائه به فعليه أن يعود ويسجد معه، ولو لم يعد كان عليه أن يسجد للسهو في آخر صلاته.
[٢] قوله : إذ بنيا تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام ; حيث شرعا الصلاة معه، وأتما به من أول صلاته ; ولذا لا يجوز الاقتداء بالمسبوق ; لأنه مقتدِ في التحريمية، والمقتدي لا يقتدى به.
[٣] قوله : فليسا مشتركين أداء ; أي أداء ما بقي عليهما ، فإنّه ليس لهما إمام فيما يؤديانه لا حقيقة، وهو ظاهر ، ولا حكماً ; لأنهما لم يلتزما أداء كل الصلاة مع إمامها ; ولذا أعطي لهما حكم الإنفراد فيما يؤديانه ; لأن الإمام قد فرغ من صلاته، وهو يؤدي ما فاته منفرداً.
And [the follower] is [considered] virtually [behind the imam] like the two latecomers (lahiqayn), meaning a man and a woman who followed a man, then they were overtaken by an event (invalidating wudu) and performed ablution and continued (bana), while the imam had finished. Then the woman aligned with the man, so the man's prayer became invalid. So the lahiq, even though he has no imam in reality, has an imam virtually (hukman), because he committed to performing all of his prayer behind the imam. So when he was overtaken by an event and performed ablution and continued, he is considered as if he is behind the imam until the rulings of followers apply to him, such as the prohibition of recitation and the like, unlike the masbuq: he is the one who caught the end of the imam's prayer, and did not commit to performing all [of his prayer] behind the imam. So with regard to what he did not catch with the imam, he is alone (munfarid), so recitation becomes obligatory for him. Thus, even if two masbuqs are partners in the opening takbir (tahrimah) because they built their tahrimah on the imam's tahrimah, they are not partners in performance. So if a woman aligned with a man in performing what he missed, the man's prayer is not invalidated due to lack of partnership in performance.
[1] His saying: 'they were overtaken by an event': i.e., an event that invalidates wudu occurred to them during the prayer, so they went to perform ablution while the imam had finished his prayer. Then they came and continued, i.e., they prayed the remainder of their prayer, each separately, as is the ruling of the lahiq.
[2] His saying: 'he committed': because he entered with him as a follower from the beginning of his prayer, intending to perform all of it with him, but that did not happen for him due to an excuse that occurred without his choice.
[3] His saying: 'is considered': in the passive form, i.e., it is considered legally that he is behind the imam, so he has an imam virtually.
[4] His saying: 'until... etc.': a branch of his being behind the imam virtually.
[0] His saying: 'such as the prohibition of recitation': in using 'prohibition' there is leniency, for recitation of the Quran for the follower according to our imams is disliked (makruh), not prohibited (haram). But since they stated that the dislike is tanzihi (close to prohibition), they applied 'prohibition' to it due to its closeness.
[6] His saying: 'and the like': meaning other rulings established for the one who catches the imam (mudrik). So he does not perform prostration of forgetfulness for what he forgets in what he performs, and his obligation does not change by his intention of residency during his prayer if he was a traveler. And it differs from him if the opposite occurs, it is valid. So if he slept in the third [rak'ah] and woke in the fourth, he performs the third without recitation. When he finishes it, he prays the fourth with the imam. If the imam finished it, he prays it alone without recitation also. If he followed the imam and then made up the third after the imam's salam, it is valid but he sins. See: Radd al-Muhtar (1:595), etc.
[1] His saying: 'alone': i.e., in reality and virtually also. Therefore the masbuq recites the Quran, seeks refuge, and praises. Exceptions to this are detailed in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Fath al-Qadir, etc., for in these he is not in the ruling of the munfarid in some aspects: 1. It is not permissible to follow him (i.e., the masbuq), unlike the munfarid. 2. If he says takbir intending to resume his prayer and cut it off, he becomes a resumer and cutter of the first, unlike the munfarid. 3. If he stands to make up what he missed and the imam has two prostrations of forgetfulness, and if this was before his following him, then he must return and prostrate with him; if he does not return, he must prostrate for forgetfulness at the end of his prayer.
[2] His saying: 'because they built their tahrimah on the imam's tahrimah': because they began the prayer with him and completed with him from the beginning of their prayer. Therefore it is not permissible to follow the masbuq, because he is a follower in the tahrimah, and a follower is not followed.
[3] His saying: 'they are not partners in performance': i.e., in performing what remains of their prayer. For they have no imam in what they perform, neither in reality, which is apparent, nor virtually, because they did not commit to performing the entire prayer with their imam. Therefore they are given the ruling of being alone in what they perform, because the imam has finished his prayer, and he performs what he missed alone.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage defines and distinguishes between two types of latecomers in congregational prayer: al-lahiq and al-masbuq. The lahiq is someone who started the prayer with the imam from the beginning but was delayed by an excusable interruption (like loss of wudu) and then returns to complete his prayer. Even though he is not physically behind the imam, he is legally (hukman) considered a follower, because he originally committed to performing all his prayer behind the imam. Hence, rulings of a follower apply to him: he must not recite behind the imam, etc. The masbuq, on the other hand, missed some rak'ahs of the imam's prayer and joins late. He did not commit to performing all his prayer behind the imam; therefore, in what he performs alone (the missed rak'ahs), he is like a munfarid (individual worshipper). He must recite, and other rulings of the munfarid apply, with some exceptions (e.g., he cannot be followed, and his intention of residency affects his prayer differently). The passage also explains a scenario: if two lahiqs (a man and a woman) return after the imam has finished, and the woman aligns with the man, the man's prayer becomes invalid because they are considered partners in performance (since both are still followers virtually). But if two masbuqs align, the man's prayer is not invalidated because they are not partners in performance; each performs his missed rak'ahs alone. The commentary clarifies that the prohibition of recitation is actually a disliked (makruh tanzihi) act, not haram, but the term 'prohibition' is used loosely. Additionally, the masbuq's prayer has unique rulings: he does not perform sajda sahw for mistakes in his missed rak'ahs (since he is alone in them), and his obligation (qasr/iftaa) can change if he intends residency during his prayer. The passage also lists exceptions where the masbuq is not considered a pure munfarid, e.g., it is not allowed to follow him, and his takbir with intention to cut the prayer has a different effect. Finally, it clarifies that two masbuqs are only partners in the opening takbir (tahrimah) but not in performance.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): A person who started the prayer with the imam from the beginning but was interrupted by a valid excuse (like loss of wudu) and later returns to complete the prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that enters one into the state of prayer and prohibits actions outside of prayer.
مقتدٍ (muqtadi): A follower in congregational prayer who is praying behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person starts praying Isha behind an imam. During the first rak'ah, he loses his wudu and goes to make it. He returns after the imam has finished the prayer. How should he complete his prayer?
A) He must recite al-Fatihah and a surah in each of his remaining rak'ahs.
B) He should not recite and just pray silently as a follower.
C) He must repeat the entire prayer because his wudu invalidated.
D) He should pray his remaining rak'ahs as if he is a munfarid.

Key Takeaway
The lahiq, despite interruption, retains follower status virtually and must observe follower rulings.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Masbuq: Latecomer's Rulings and Exceptions
Defines al-masbuq and his rulings, including exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-masbuq, explain why he must recite in his missed rak'ahs, and list the exceptions where he differs from a munfarid.

Core Idea
The masbuq is like a munfarid in his missed rak'ahs, but with key exceptions that reinforce his connection to the imam's tahrimah.

When a person joins the congregation late, missing some rak'ahs, he becomes a masbuq. Unlike the lahiq, he did not commit to performing all his prayer behind the imam. Thus, for the rak'ahs he performs alone, he must recite like a munfarid. Yet, the Hanafi school outlines important exceptions where he differs from a true munfarid, as detailed in the passage. This lesson explores those rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the masbuq's defining feature
He joined after the imam started, missing one or more rak'ahs, and caught only part of the prayer.
He is distinct from the lahiq who started from the beginning.
2
Understand his legal status
He did not commit to performing all prayer behind the imam. Therefore, in his missed rak'ahs, he is like a munfarid (hukman and haqiqatan).
The term 'munfarid' here includes both reality and ruling, except for specific exceptions.
3
Note the consequences of being like a munfarid
He must recite al-Fatihah and a surah in his missed rak'ahs. He does not perform sajdah sahw for mistakes in those rak'ahs.
The passage explicitly says: 'so recitation becomes obligatory for him'.
4
Recognize the exceptions
Despite being like a munfarid, the masbuq cannot be followed as an imam; his intention to cut prayer has the effect of cutting both prayers; and he must return to the imam if the imam performs sajdah sahw before the masbuq separates.
These exceptions show that his prayer remains tied to the imam's tahrimah.
5
Apply to the alignment scenario
Two masbuqs are not partners in performance of their missed rak'ahs. If they align, no invalidation occurs, unlike lahiqs.
The woman-man alignment example shows this clearly.

وإما حُكْماً كاللاحقين يعني رجل وامرأة اقتديا برجل فسبقهما حدث فتوضئا وبنيا، وقد فَرَغَ الإمام ، فحاذت المرأةُ الرَّجلَ فسدت صلاةُ الرَّجل. فاللاحق وإن لم يكن له إمام حقيقة ، فله إمام حكماً، فإنَّه التزم أن يؤدِّي جميع صلاتِه خَلْفَ الإمام ، فإذا سبقَهُ الحدث فتوضأ وبنا، يُجْعَل كأَنَّه خَلْفَ الإمام حتَّى يثبت له أحكامُ المقتديين كحرمة القراءة، ونحوها بخلاف المسبوق : وهو الذي أدرك آخر صلاة الإمام، فلم يلتزم أداءَ الكُلِّ خَلْفَ الإمام . فهو في أداء ما لم يُدْرِكْهُ مع الإمام منفرد حتَّى تَجِبَ عليه القراءة، فالمسبوقان وإن كانا مشتركين في التَّحريمةِ إذ بنيا تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام، فليسا مشتركين أداء، فإن حاذت المرأةُ رجلاً في أداء ما سبق، لم تفسد صلاة الرجل ؛ لعدم الشركة في الأداء.
[۱]قوله : فسبقهما ؛ أي عرض لهما حدث ناقض للوضوء في أثناء الصلاة، فذهبا للتوضؤ وقد فرغ الإمام عن صلاته، فجاءا فبنيا ؛ أي صليا ما بقي من صلاتهما كل واحد منهما على حدة كما هو حكم اللاحق.
[٢]قوله : فإنه التزم ؛ حيث دخل معه مقتدياً من أول صلاته، وقصد أن يؤدي معه كلّها إلا أنه لم يحصل له ذلك ؛ لعذر لحقه بدون اختياره.
[٣]قوله : يجعل ؛ بصيغة المجهول ؛ أي يجعل شرعاً أنه خلف الإمام، فكان له إماماً حكماً.
[٤]قوله : حتى...الخ ؛ تفريع على كونه خلف الإمام حكماً.
[0]قوله : كحرمة القراءة ؛ في إطلاق الحرمة مسامحة، فإن قراءة القرآن للمقتدي عند أصحابنا مكروهة لا حرام، لكن لما صرَّحوا أنّ الكراهة تحريمية أطلق عليها الحرمة؛ لقربها منها.
[٦] قوله : ونحوها ؛ أي غيرها من الأحكام الثابتة للمدرك ، فلا يأتي بسجدة سهو بما يسهو فيما يؤدّيه، ولا يتغير فرضُهُ بنيّة إقامته في أثناء صلاته إن كان مسافرا، ويخالفه لو عكسه يصح ، فلو نام في الثالثة واستيقظ في الرابعة . فإنه يأتي بالثالثة بلا قراءة . فإذا فرغ منها صلى مع الإمام الرابعة ، وإن فرغ منها الإمام صلاها وحده بلا قراءة أيضا ؛ فلو تابع الإمام ثم قضى الثالثة بعد سلام الإمام صح وأثم. ينظر : رد المحتار» (١ : ٥٩٥)، وغيره.
[١]قوله : منفرد ؛ أي حقيقة وحكماً أيضاً ؛ ولذا يقرأ المسبوق القرآن، ويتعوذ ويثني، وتستثنى منه أحكام على ما بسطه في (الدر المختار» و«فتح القدير» وغيرها، فإنه فيها ليس في حكم المنفرد :
١. منها : أنه لا يجوز الاقتداء به بخلاف المنفرد.
٢. ومنها : أنه لو كبر ينوي استئناف صلاته وقطعها يصير مستأنفاً وقاطعاً للأولى، بخلاف المنفرد.
٣. ومنها : أنه لو قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به وعلى الإمام سجدتا سهو، ولو كان قبل اقتدائه به فعليه أن يعود ويسجد معه، ولو لم يعد كان عليه أن يسجد للسهو في آخر صلاته.
[٢] قوله : إذ بنيا تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام ; حيث شرعا الصلاة معه، وأتما به من أول صلاته ; ولذا لا يجوز الاقتداء بالمسبوق ; لأنه مقتدِ في التحريمية، والمقتدي لا يقتدى به.
[٣] قوله : فليسا مشتركين أداء ; أي أداء ما بقي عليهما ، فإنّه ليس لهما إمام فيما يؤديانه لا حقيقة، وهو ظاهر ، ولا حكماً ; لأنهما لم يلتزما أداء كل الصلاة مع إمامها ; ولذا أعطي لهما حكم الإنفراد فيما يؤديانه ; لأن الإمام قد فرغ من صلاته، وهو يؤدي ما فاته منفرداً.
And [the follower] is [considered] virtually [behind the imam] like the two latecomers (lahiqayn), meaning a man and a woman who followed a man, then they were overtaken by an event (invalidating wudu) and performed ablution and continued (bana), while the imam had finished. Then the woman aligned with the man, so the man's prayer became invalid. So the lahiq, even though he has no imam in reality, has an imam virtually (hukman), because he committed to performing all of his prayer behind the imam. So when he was overtaken by an event and performed ablution and continued, he is considered as if he is behind the imam until the rulings of followers apply to him, such as the prohibition of recitation and the like, unlike the masbuq: he is the one who caught the end of the imam's prayer, and did not commit to performing all [of his prayer] behind the imam. So with regard to what he did not catch with the imam, he is alone (munfarid), so recitation becomes obligatory for him. Thus, even if two masbuqs are partners in the opening takbir (tahrimah) because they built their tahrimah on the imam's tahrimah, they are not partners in performance. So if a woman aligned with a man in performing what he missed, the man's prayer is not invalidated due to lack of partnership in performance.
[1] His saying: 'they were overtaken by an event': i.e., an event that invalidates wudu occurred to them during the prayer, so they went to perform ablution while the imam had finished his prayer. Then they came and continued, i.e., they prayed the remainder of their prayer, each separately, as is the ruling of the lahiq.
[2] His saying: 'he committed': because he entered with him as a follower from the beginning of his prayer, intending to perform all of it with him, but that did not happen for him due to an excuse that occurred without his choice.
[3] His saying: 'is considered': in the passive form, i.e., it is considered legally that he is behind the imam, so he has an imam virtually.
[4] His saying: 'until... etc.': a branch of his being behind the imam virtually.
[0] His saying: 'such as the prohibition of recitation': in using 'prohibition' there is leniency, for recitation of the Quran for the follower according to our imams is disliked (makruh), not prohibited (haram). But since they stated that the dislike is tanzihi (close to prohibition), they applied 'prohibition' to it due to its closeness.
[6] His saying: 'and the like': meaning other rulings established for the one who catches the imam (mudrik). So he does not perform prostration of forgetfulness for what he forgets in what he performs, and his obligation does not change by his intention of residency during his prayer if he was a traveler. And it differs from him if the opposite occurs, it is valid. So if he slept in the third [rak'ah] and woke in the fourth, he performs the third without recitation. When he finishes it, he prays the fourth with the imam. If the imam finished it, he prays it alone without recitation also. If he followed the imam and then made up the third after the imam's salam, it is valid but he sins. See: Radd al-Muhtar (1:595), etc.
[1] His saying: 'alone': i.e., in reality and virtually also. Therefore the masbuq recites the Quran, seeks refuge, and praises. Exceptions to this are detailed in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, Fath al-Qadir, etc., for in these he is not in the ruling of the munfarid in some aspects: 1. It is not permissible to follow him (i.e., the masbuq), unlike the munfarid. 2. If he says takbir intending to resume his prayer and cut it off, he becomes a resumer and cutter of the first, unlike the munfarid. 3. If he stands to make up what he missed and the imam has two prostrations of forgetfulness, and if this was before his following him, then he must return and prostrate with him; if he does not return, he must prostrate for forgetfulness at the end of his prayer.
[2] His saying: 'because they built their tahrimah on the imam's tahrimah': because they began the prayer with him and completed with him from the beginning of their prayer. Therefore it is not permissible to follow the masbuq, because he is a follower in the tahrimah, and a follower is not followed.
[3] His saying: 'they are not partners in performance': i.e., in performing what remains of their prayer. For they have no imam in what they perform, neither in reality, which is apparent, nor virtually, because they did not commit to performing the entire prayer with their imam. Therefore they are given the ruling of being alone in what they perform, because the imam has finished his prayer, and he performs what he missed alone.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage defines and distinguishes between two types of latecomers in congregational prayer: al-lahiq and al-masbuq. The lahiq is someone who started the prayer with the imam from the beginning but was delayed by an excusable interruption (like loss of wudu) and then returns to complete his prayer. Even though he is not physically behind the imam, he is legally (hukman) considered a follower, because he originally committed to performing all his prayer behind the imam. Hence, rulings of a follower apply to him: he must not recite behind the imam, etc. The masbuq, on the other hand, missed some rak'ahs of the imam's prayer and joins late. He did not commit to performing all his prayer behind the imam; therefore, in what he performs alone (the missed rak'ahs), he is like a munfarid (individual worshipper). He must recite, and other rulings of the munfarid apply, with some exceptions (e.g., he cannot be followed, and his intention of residency affects his prayer differently). The passage also explains a scenario: if two lahiqs (a man and a woman) return after the imam has finished, and the woman aligns with the man, the man's prayer becomes invalid because they are considered partners in performance (since both are still followers virtually). But if two masbuqs align, the man's prayer is not invalidated because they are not partners in performance; each performs his missed rak'ahs alone. The commentary clarifies that the prohibition of recitation is actually a disliked (makruh tanzihi) act, not haram, but the term 'prohibition' is used loosely. Additionally, the masbuq's prayer has unique rulings: he does not perform sajda sahw for mistakes in his missed rak'ahs (since he is alone in them), and his obligation (qasr/iftaa) can change if he intends residency during his prayer. The passage also lists exceptions where the masbuq is not considered a pure munfarid, e.g., it is not allowed to follow him, and his takbir with intention to cut the prayer has a different effect. Finally, it clarifies that two masbuqs are only partners in the opening takbir (tahrimah) but not in performance.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joined the congregation after the imam has already started, missing one or more rak'ahs. He catches the imam in the last part of the prayer.
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation. Rulings like obligatory recitation apply.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that enters one into the state of prayer and prohibits actions outside of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man joins the congregation when the imam is in the second rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer. After the imam says the final salam, how many rak'ahs must the man pray on his own, and is recitation obligatory?
A) 2 rak'ahs, recitation not obligatory.
B) 2 rak'ahs, recitation obligatory.
C) 3 rak'ahs, recitation obligatory.
D) 1 rak'ah, recitation not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq is like a munfarid in his missed rak'ahs, making recitation wajib, but with exceptions that connect him to the imam's tahrimah.

The Masbuq's Performance: Individual in What He Missed
Ruling statement with commentary expansion on the masbuq's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the masbuq is treated as an individual (munfarid) in the portion he performs after the imam and identify the exceptions where he differs from a true munfarid.

Core Idea
A latecomer to prayer (masbuq) is like an individual in the missed rak'ahs, but with key exceptions.

When you join the congregational prayer late, you become responsible for the parts you missed. The Hanafi school teaches that for those missed portions, you are like a person praying alone (munfarid). This lesson explores that principle and its exceptions, as explained by classical Hanafi scholars in the commentary on al-Wiqayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage first states that the masbuq is an individual (munfarid) in performing what he missed. This means he must recite the Quran in those rak'ahs because recitation is wajib for a munfarid.
The ruling is that recitation becomes wajib upon the masbuq in the missed portion.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is implicit: the general obligation of recitation for anyone not led by an imam. Since the imam's recitation only covers the portion he led, the missed part requires the masbuq's own recitation.
This is based on the principle that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower only for what is performed together.
3
Note the Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that if the masbuq catches the ruku' with the imam, he does not need to recite in the missed rak'ahs. The Hanafi school insists on recitation because the masbuq is like an individual in performance.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
4
Expand through Commentary
The commentary lists three exceptions where the masbuq is not treated as a true munfarid: (1) he cannot be followed, (2) his intention to cut off prayer has a different effect, (3) he must return to the imam for sajdat al-sahw under certain conditions.
These exceptions show that the similarity is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهو في أداء ما لم يُدْرِكْهُ مع الإمام منفرد حتَّى تَجِبَ عليه القراءة، فالمسبوقان وإن كانا مشتركين في التَّحريمةِ إذ بنيا تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام، فليسا مشتركين أداء، فإن حاذت المرأةُ رجلاً في أداء ما سبق، لم تفسد صلاة الرجل ؛ لعدم الشركة في الأداء. المسبوق في هذه الأحكام، فإنّه يقرأ فيما يؤديه، ويأتي بسجدة السهو إن سها فيه، ويتغير فرضُهُ بقصد الإقامة فيه، وبينهما فروق أخر أيضاً مذكورة في «الأشباه») ، و«النهر» ، وليطلب تفصيل ذلك من «السعاية». (۲) [١]قوله : منفرد ؛ أي حقيقة وحكماً أيضاً ؛ ولذا يقرأ المسبوق القرآن، ويتعوذ ويثني، وتستثنى منه أحكام على ما بسطه في (الدر المختار)(۳) و«فتح القدير» وغيرها، فإنه فيها ليس في حكم المنفرد : ١. منها : أنه لا يجوز الاقتداء به بخلاف المنفرد. ٢. ومنها : أنه لو كبر ينوي استئناف صلاته وقطعها يصير مستأنفاً وقاطعاً للأولى، بخلاف المنفرد. . ومنها : أنه لو قام إلى قضاء ما سبق به وعلى الإمام سجدتا سهو، ولو كان قبل اقتدائه به فعليه أن يعود ويسجد معه، ولو لم يعد كان عليه أن يسجد للسهو في آخر صلاته. [٢] قوله : إذ بنيا تحريمتهما على تحريمة الإمام ؛ حيث شرعا الصلاة معه، وأتما به من أول صلاته ؛ ولذا لا يجوز الاقتداء بالمسبوق ؛ لأنه مقتدِ في التحريمية، والمقتدي لا يقتدى به. [٣] قوله : فليسا مشتركين أداء ؛ أي أداء ما بقي عليهما ، فإنّه ليس لهما إمام فيما يؤديانه لا حقيقة، وهو ظاهر ، ولا حكماً ؛ لأنهما لم يلتزما أداء كل الصلاة مع إمامها ؛ ولذا أعطي لهما حكم الإنفراد فيما يؤديانه ؛ لأن الإمام قد فرغ من صلاته، وهو يؤدي ما فاته منفرداً.
So he is, in performing what he did not catch up with the imam, an individual (munfarid) such that recitation becomes obligatory upon him. Two latecomers (masbuqan), even though they share in the tahrimah (opening takbir) since they build their tahrimah upon the imam's tahrimah, are not sharing in performance (ada'). If a woman aligns with a man in performing what preceded, the man's prayer is not invalidated due to the lack of sharing in performance. The masbuq, in these rulings, recites in what he performs, performs the prostration of forgetfulness if he errs in it, and his obligation changes by intending residence (iqamah) in it, and there are other differences between them mentioned in al-Ashbah and al-Nahr, and the details should be sought from al-Si'ayah. (2) [1] His saying 'individual': meaning in reality and in ruling as well; hence the masbuq recites the Quran, seeks refuge, and praises, and from it are excepted rulings as detailed in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Fath al-Qadir and others, for in them he is not in the ruling of an individual: 1. Among them: that it is not permissible to follow him (iqtida') unlike an individual. 2. Among them: that if he says takbir intending to restart his prayer and cut it off, he becomes a restarter and cutter of the first, unlike an individual. 3. Among them: that if he stands to make up what preceded while the imam has two prostrations of forgetfulness, and if it was before his following him, he must return and prostrate with him, and if he does not return, he must perform the prostration of forgetfulness at the end of his prayer. [2] His saying 'since they build their tahrimah upon the imam's tahrimah': because they began prayer with him and completed with him from the start of their prayer; hence it is not permissible to follow a masbuq because he is a follower in the tahrimah, and a follower is not followed. [3] His saying 'are not sharing in performance': meaning performance of what remains upon them; for they have no imam in what they perform, neither in reality, which is apparent, nor in ruling; because they did not commit to performing the entire prayer with their imam; hence they are given the ruling of individuality in what they perform, because the imam has completed his prayer, and he performs what he missed individually.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn and its commentary explaining the status of a latecomer (masbuq) in congregational prayer. The author states that for the portion of prayer the masbuq performs after the imam has completed, he is like a person praying alone (munfarid). Consequently, recitation of Quran becomes obligatory upon him, as it is for a munfarid. Even if two latecomers both followed the same imam and share in the opening takbir (tahrimah), they do not share in the performance (ada') of the parts they missed. Therefore, if a woman aligns with a man in that portion, it does not invalidate the man's prayer because there is no sharing in performance. The masbuq recites, performs sajdat al-sahw if he errs, and his obligation changes if he intends iqamah (residence). The commentary clarifies that 'munfarid' means both in reality and in ruling, and then lists three exceptions from al-Durr al-Mukhtar where the masbuq is not treated as a munfarid: (1) It is not permissible for another to follow the masbuq (unlike a true munfarid); (2) If the masbuq makes a takbir intending to restart his prayer and cut it off, he actually becomes a restarter and cutter (unlike a munfarid whose intention to cut off would invalidate but not make him restart); (3) If the imam makes sajdat al-sahw while the masbuq has stood up to make up what he missed, the masbuq must return and prostrate with him if the imam's sajda occurred before the masbuq finished his iqtida', otherwise he makes sajda later. The reason for not sharing in performance is that neither has an imam in what they perform, neither in reality nor in ruling, because they did not undertake to perform the entire prayer behind the imam.

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer after the imam has already begun, and thus misses part of the prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) which makes the prayer start and prohibits actions outside prayer.
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the masbuq have to recite the Quran in the rak'ahs he performs after the imam has finished?
A) Because he is following another masbuq
B) Because he shares in the tahrimah with the imam
C) Because he is like a munfarid in that portion
D) Because the imam did not recite

Key Takeaway
The masbuq is like an individual in the missed rak'ahs, but with exceptions: he cannot be followed, his intention to cut off differs, and he must return for the imam's sajdat al-sahw.
