The Ruling on Hadath During Prayer: Building vs. Restarting
Explains the ruling of hadath during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building after hadath, identify the conditions for valid building, and explain the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Building after hadath is permitted under conditions; the prayer is not considered complete until salām.

In this passage, we explore what happens when a person is overtaken by hadath (an event nullifying wudu) during prayer. The Hanafi school permits building (bināʾ)—resuming the prayer from where it was interrupted after performing wudu—but only under specific conditions. We also examine the internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and the external dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires restarting the prayer entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and its scope
Determine the initial ruling: if hadath overtakes you, perform wudu and either build or restart. Scope: only unintentional, wudu-breaking, physical exit hadath. Exclude intentional hadath, ihtilam, fainting, etc.
2
Analyze the conditions for valid building
List the four conditions: (1) no pause equal to a rukn, (2) no contradictory action while going/returning, (3) no unnecessary distant water source, (4) no delay after wudu. Understand why each preserves the continuity of prayer.
These conditions ensure the prayer remains valid if building is chosen.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on tashahhud
Contrast Abu Hanifa's view (prayer incomplete until salām, so building allowed after tashahhud) with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's view (sitting for tashahhud completes prayer, so no building after). Note the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i
State Shafi'i's proof (hadith commanding restart) and his qiyas argument. Explain the Hanafi response: the hadith is interpreted as conditional or recommendatory due to other narrations allowing building.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis may build; Shafi'is must restart.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a person has hadath, performs wudu, then speaks while returning), determine if building is valid and cite the violated condition.
This integrates all conditions and disputes.

Chapter on Hadath in Prayer. A praying person whom hadath overtakes performs wudu and completes his prayer. [1] He said: 'Chapter on hadath in prayer' – a beginning in mentioning the accidental occurrences that happen in prayer. [2] He said: 'Chapter on hadath in prayer' – that is, this chapter is about expounding the rulings of hadath occurring in prayer. [3] He said: 'overtakes him' – in it is an indication that what permits deputization and building is the hadath that occurs to him during his prayer without his choice, without his intention for the hadath or its cause, and likewise from other than him. So intentional hadath: no building upon it. Likewise if he had a wound and he pressed it in prayer so blood flowed from it, because intentional seeking of hadath is found from him. Likewise if a person threw a stone or a pellet at him and it hit him so blood flowed from it, because the hadath is from him due to someone else. Thus al-'Ayni detailed it in al-Binayah. [4] He said: 'hadath' – it is restricted by two restrictions as detailed by al-'Ayni and others from the commentators of al-Hidayah: first, that it be a hadath that nullifies wudu, so no building in the case of ihtilam during his prayer. Second, that it come out from his body, so no building in the case of his garment becoming najis above the size of a dirham, or his wudu being nullified by fainting, insanity, or loud laughter, for these are not hadath coming out from the body. [5] He said: 'performs wudu' – that is, it is obligatory upon him to depart and perform wudu, then if he wishes he completes what remains of his prayer (that is what is meant by building upon what preceded), and if he wishes he starts anew, i.e., abandons what passed and prays from the beginning. Even after tashahhud, contrary to al-Shafi'i. 'Even after tashahhud' – contrary to them (the two Sahibayn); for when he sits the measure of tashahhud his prayer is complete, according to them. And according to Abu Hanifa it is not complete, because exiting by his own action is fard according to him. [1] He said: 'contrary to al-Shafi'i' – for according to him starting anew is necessary, and building is not permitted because the prayer is invalidated by the existence of nullifiers from nullification of purity, walking, returning, and performing wudu. This is qiyas, and the hadith testifies for it: 'If one of you passes wind in prayer, let him depart, perform wudu, and repeat the prayer.' It was narrated by the authors of Sunan, Ahmad, and al-Daraqutni. According to us it is interpreted upon when a condition of validity of building is lost or as an indication of recommendation, due to narrations indicating the permissibility of building as you will come across, God willing. [2] He said: 'his prayer is complete' – due to completion of the pillars and obligations. So if he has hadath after it, he does not build, because there remains no obligation upon him. [3] He said: 'because exiting by his own action' – that is, exiting from prayer by an action contradicting prayer from the one praying, and if it is speech it is fard, and specifically the word 'al-salam' for exiting is wajib, and if... Conditions for permissibility of building: 1. That he not remain after hadath the time of performing a rukn, for if he remains it invalidates his prayer. 2. That he not perform an action contradictory to prayer during going and returning for wudu, for if he speaks, or uncovers his private parts, or intentionally has hadath during going, it invalidates. 3. That he not perform an action from which he has no alternative, for if he goes to perform wudu to a farther place while it is available in a nearer place, it invalidates. 4. That he not delay after completing wudu without excuse like crowding. Let the detail be sought in these investigations from al-Si'ayah.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the ruling on hadath (an event nullifying wudu) that occurs during prayer. The author begins by stating the base ruling: a person whom hadath overtakes during prayer should perform wudu and then complete the remaining part of his prayer. The commentary then clarifies several points. First, the hadath must be unintentional – if one intentionally causes hadath (e.g., pressing a wound so blood flows), then building is not allowed. Second, the hadath must be a wudu-breaker exiting the body; if the prayer is nullified by something like fainting (not a physical exit), building is not permitted. Third, the worshipper has the option to either build upon what he has prayed or start anew. The passage then addresses a dispute: Shafi'i holds that building is never allowed and the prayer must be restarted entirely; he cites a hadith about passing wind. The Hanafis interpret this hadith as conditional or recommendatory, not absolute. Another intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the case of hadath after tashahhud. According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is not complete until the salutation (salam) is uttered, so building is still allowed. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that sitting for the measure of tashahhud completes the prayer, so subsequent hadath does not permit building. Finally, the text lists four conditions for valid building: (1) one must not pause the length of a rukn; (2) one must not speak or otherwise invalidate the prayer during the process; (3) one must not unnecessarily go to a distant water source; and (4) one must not delay unnecessarily after wudu. These conditions ensure that the continuity of prayer is preserved as much as possible.

Key Terms
حدث (ḥadath): An event that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind, urine, or blood exiting the body.
بناء (bināʾ): To resume the prayer from the point where the ḥadath occurred after performing wudu, without starting over.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in the final sitting of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following invalidates the option to build (bināʾ) after hadath?
A) The hadath occurs after tashahhud.
B) The worshipper performs wudu at a distant water source when a nearer one is available.
C) The worshipper speaks while returning from wudu.
D) The hadath was caused intentionally by pressing a wound.

Key Takeaway
Building after hadath is permitted in Hanafi fiqh only if the hadath was unintentional, the worshipper does not pause a rukn, and does not invalidate the prayer during the process.

Building Prayer After Hadath After Tashahhud: A Three-Way Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute with conditions for building permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on building prayer after hadath after tashahhud, identify the four conditions for its validity, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Building prayer after hadath after tashahhud is required because the act of exiting remains an obligation.

This passage examines a three-way legal dispute regarding whether a prayer can be resumed after ritual impurity (hadath) occurs in the final sitting after tashahhud. Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer is incomplete because exiting by one's own act (khurūj bi-ṣunʿihi) is still obligatory, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider the prayer complete. The Shafi'i school argues that the prayer is entirely invalid and must be restarted. The Hanafi school lays out specific conditions under which building is permitted, using istihsan and ta'wil to reconcile conflicting hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions on building after hadath after tashahhud
Recognize that Abu Hanifa requires building, Sahibayn consider prayer complete (no building), and al-Shafi'i demands a fresh start.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's key argument: the obligation of exiting by one's own act (khurūj bi-ṣunʿihi)
Abu Hanifa considers the act of exiting prayer (e.g., saying salam) to be a fard obligation. After tashahhud, the pillars are complete but this exit obligation remains. Therefore, hadath does not invalidate the prayer; the prayer is incomplete and must be completed after wudu.
This is the core difference with Sahibayn, who consider the prayer complete and thus no building needed.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith of passing wind and qiyas
The Shafi'i school relies on a hadith commanding one to leave, perform wudu, and repeat the prayer. They also use qiyas: any nullifier of wudu invalidates prayer, so building is not permissible.
The hadith is cited as 'If one of you passes wind during prayer, let him leave, perform wudu, and repeat the prayer.'
4
Examine the Hanafi response: ta'wil and istihsan
Hanafi scholars interpret the hadith as conditional on missing one of the four conditions for building (e.g., remaining too long), or as indicating recommendation (istihbab) rather than obligation. They cite other narrations that allow building, and prefer istihsan over qiyas.
This shows the Hanafi method of textual interpretation and preference for istihsan when qiyas conflicts with maslaha or other evidence.
5
List the four conditions for building to be valid according to the Hanafi school
The passage explicitly states four shurut: (1) not remaining after hadath for the duration of performing a rukn; (2) not performing any act conflicting with prayer while going/returning; (3) going to the nearest water source; (4) not delaying after finishing wudu without a valid excuse.
If any condition is violated, the prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether a prayer can be built upon after hadath occurs after tashahhud. Abu Hanifa holds that building is required because the obligation of exiting by one's own act still remains. Sahibayn hold that the prayer is complete and no building is needed. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the prayer is invalid and must be restarted. The author then lists conditions for building per Hanafi: (1) not remaining for the duration of a rukn, (2) not performing a conflicting act, (3) going to the nearest water, (4) not delaying after wudu. Then the text addresses Shafi'i's proof from the hadith of passing wind, interpreting it as either missing a condition or as recommended, and noting that other narrations support building. This shows the Hanafi method of ta'wil and istihsan over qiyas.

Key Terms
البناء (al-binā'): Completing the prayer after an invalidating event by performing wudu and returning to the prayer state.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony recited in the final sitting of prayer.
الحدث (al-hadath): Anything that nullifies wudu.
الخروج بصنعه (al-khurūj bi-ṣunʿihi): Exiting the prayer by one's own deliberate act, e.g., saying salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a condition for building a prayer after hadath after tashahhud?
A) The person must speak during wudu.
B) The person must go to the farthest water source.
C) The person must not remain after hadath for the duration of a rukn.
D) The person must delay returning after wudu.

Key Takeaway
Building after hadath after tashahhud is required in the Hanafi school because the obligation of exiting by one's own act remains, and it is valid only if four conditions are met.

Building After Hadath During Prayer: Imām and Individual
Explanation of choices for imām and individual after hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the options available to an imām or individual who experiences hadath after tashahhud, and state why renewal is considered better.

Core Idea
If hadath occurs after tashahhud, building is permissible but renewal is better.

When a worshipper experiences ritual impurity during prayer, especially after tashahhud, the Hanafi school provides specific guidance. For the imām, he must first delegate leadership to another person before performing wudu. Then he may choose to complete his prayer where he performed wudu or return to his original place. The individual has a similar choice. This lesson examines these options and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
State that renewal (istī'naf) is considered better, but building (binā') is permissible for both imām and munfarid after hadath post-tashahhud.
2
Explain the imām's required delegation
The imām must first pull (yajurru) another person forward to lead the remainder of the prayer. This is called istikhāf. Then he performs wudu.
If he speaks while delegating, his prayer becomes invalid.
3
Analyse the imām's two options after wudu
He may either return to his original place (returning) or complete the prayer where he performed wudu. The choice is based on convenience: less walking vs. unity of place.
He may incline to whichever he wishes.
4
Apply the same options to the individual
Similarly, the munfarid (individual) may complete where he performed wudu or return. The rule is the same because an obligation (exiting the prayer by his choice) remains upon him.
5
Note the consequence of improper delegation
If the imām fails to delegate and leaves the mosque, the congregation's prayer becomes invalid unless there are connected rows outside.
This underscores the importance of maintaining continuity.

Commentary
This passage explains the matn's statement that renewal is better but building is permissible. For the imām, if hadath occurs, he should pull a person forward to lead the rest, then go for wudu and either return or complete where he did wudu. The choice is based on precedent: less walking vs. unity of place. For the individual, similar option. The commentary also clarifies that if the imām fails to delegate and leaves, the congregation's prayer becomes invalid if no connected rows outside. This shows the importance of maintaining continuity of prayer as a congregation.

Key Terms
يجر (yajurru): He pulls or draws another person to his place to lead the remainder of the prayer.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhāf): Delegation of imamate to another person during prayer.
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The follower in congregational prayer.
المنفرد (al-munfarid): An individual praying alone.

Key Takeaway

Hadath in Prayer: Options for Imam, Individual, and Follower
Rulings and options for the one who experiences hadath during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the imam, munfarid, and muqtadi when hadath occurs, and apply the preferred option of isti'naf versus building.

Core Idea
When hadath strikes, isti'naf is better, but building is permissible; the imam may appoint a substitute or choose.

Prayer is a pillar of faith, but what happens when a sudden hadath (ritual impurity) breaks your wudu in the middle of salah? This lesson from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah unpacks the Hanafi guidelines for three roles: the imam leading the prayer, the individual praying alone, and the follower. You will learn that you are not forced to restart from scratch – you have options, and the school gives you a choice based on virtue and necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the roles and the core ruling
First, distinguish between the imam, munfarid (individual), and muqtadi (follower). The passage opens by stating that isti'naf (starting anew) is afdal (better) for all. Understand that this is a recommended, not required, action.
Isti'naf means intentionally cutting the current prayer and starting over after wudu.
2
Analyze the imam's options: istikhlaf and choice
The imam may appoint a substitute (istikhlaf) by pulling another person to his place via gesture (not speech). After wudu, he may either complete the prayer in the place of wudu or return to the original spot. Both are permissible; he chooses based on preference.
If he leaves without appointing a substitute and there are no connected rows, the congregation's prayer is invalid.
3
Apply the same analysis to the munfarid
The munfarid has the same two options: complete where he made wudu or return. However, if hadath occurs after tashahhud, building (bina') is permissible because the only remaining obligation is the voluntary exit.
Building means continuing the same prayer from where he stopped after wudu, not starting over.
4
Determine the muqtadi's ruling
The follower's ruling depends on whether his imam (the substitute) has finished the prayer. If the imam has finished, the follower may complete where he made wudu or return. If not, he must return and complete behind the substitute. If a barrier (e.g., river) exists that prevents valid following, he must return if possible; otherwise he may choose.
Returning is obligatory when the barrier would invalidate following the substitute imam.
5
Examine special cases: madness, fainting, and wet dream
Madness and fainting invalidate wudu, so they trigger the same options. A wet dream during prayer is possible only if one sleeps in a manner that does not break wudu (e.g., sleep in ruku' or sujud). In all cases, the person may choose to build or start anew.
The wet dream scenario is rare but shows Hanafi precision: sleep that does not nullify wudu allows the prayer to continue until a wet dream occurs.

Book of Prayer / Hadath in Prayer. And starting anew is better, and the Imam brings another to his place, then performs ablution and completes there, or returns, and likewise the one praying alone. (And starting anew is better). When he mentioned a general ruling encompassing all worshippers, he detailed the ruling for each of the Imam, the one praying alone, and the follower, saying: (The Imam brings another to his place): this is the interpretation of appointment of a substitute, then he performs ablution and completes there, or returns: meaning if he wishes he completes where he performed ablution, and if he wishes he performs ablution and returns to the first place. He was given a choice because in the first there is less walking, and in the second performing prayer in one place, so he inclines to whichever he wishes. And likewise the one praying alone: meaning if he wishes he completes where he performed ablution. If hadath overtakes him after tashahhud, building is permissible for him because there remains an obligation upon him, which is exiting the prayer by his choice. [1] His saying: 'yajurru' – with a damma on the jim and tashdid on the ra – meaning he pulls another man to his place, by taking his garment or gesturing to him and informing him of what remains of his prayer by gesture, and if by speech his prayer is invalidated. And if he does not appoint a substitute and exits the mosque, the prayer of the people is invalidated if there are no connected rows outside the mosque. So in al-Binayah. [2] His saying: 'ada' – because walking back and forth is forgiven by the Lawgiver due to necessity. [3] His saying: 'khiyyir' – from al-takhyir; i.e. between building there or here. [4] His saying: 'yamīlu ilā ayyihimā shāa' – because in each there is virtue from one aspect and lack thereof from another, so he is given choice between them. (1) Meaning of isti'naf: to do an action that cuts the prayer, then begin after ablution. See: Hashiyat al-Shalabi ala al-Tabyin (1:145). (2) To avoid the semblance of dispute, and it is said: the one praying alone starts anew, while the Imam and follower build out of preservation of the virtue of congregation. See: al-Hidayah (1:331). (3) And it is the choice of Shaykh al-Islam and Imam al-Sarakhsi, and it is better. See: Majma' al-Anhur (1:114). (4) In the second is less walking, and it is the choice of some. See: Majma' al-Anhur (1:114). (5) al-Binayah (2:371). 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. If his imam has finished, and if not he returns, and likewise the follower. And even if he goes mad, or faints, or has a wet dream, and if he wishes he returns. (His saying: 'if his imam has finished') is connected to his saying: 'he completes there or returns', and the pronoun in 'his imam' refers to the first imam, and his imam is the one he appointed as substitute, for the substitute is imam for the first imam and the people. (And if not he returns): meaning if his imam, i.e. the substitute, has not finished, the imam returns and completes behind his substitute. [2] (And likewise the follower): meaning if his imam has finished he completes there or returns, and if he has not finished he returns. (And even if he goes mad, or faints, or has a wet dream): meaning he sleeps in his prayer a sleep that does not invalidate his wudu, then he has a wet dream. [4] [1] His saying: 'ada': means obligatorily if there is nothing between the place of prayer and the place of his wudu that prevents the validity of following, such as a road, river, and the like. If there is, he is given choice between returning and completing in that place. [2] His saying: 'returns': necessarily if there is between him and his imam something that prevents the validity of following, and if not he does not return, and follows from there, as clarified in al-Hidayah (1:381) and al-Binayah (2:380). (3) His saying: 'even if he goes mad' – with a damma on the jim and tashdid on the nun – meaning madness occurs to him during his prayer, and it is known that madness invalidates wudu. [4] His saying: 'or faints' – in the passive form, and its active is not used – meaning fainting occurs to him, which in Persian is 'bihushi', and it invalidates wudu. [0] His saying: 'he sleeps' – because a misunderstanding might occur that wet dream only happens in sleep, so how can it occur during prayer? He pointed to its refutation and explained its form: that he sleeps in his prayer and has a wet dream. Then, because it might be thought that sleep itself invalidates wudu, so his wudu would be invalidated without the wet dream, he qualified it by saying: 'a sleep that does not invalidate his wudu'; meaning he slept in his prayer in a state that does not invalidate his wudu, such as sleep during ruku' and sujud, and had a wet dream. And if the author said 'or he emitted semen', it would have been... (1) al-Hidayah (1:381). (2) al-Binayah (2:380).
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah deals with the rulings for an imam, one praying alone (munfarid), and a follower (muqtadi) when they experience hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer. The author first states that starting the prayer anew (isti'naf) is better (afdal) than building upon the existing prayer. Then details the options for the imam: he may appoint a substitute (istikhlaf) by bringing another person to his place via gesture (not speech), perform wudu, and either complete the prayer in that place or return to the original spot. Both options are permissible; the choice is left to him since each has a virtue (less walking vs. praying in one location). The same options apply to the one praying alone. If hadath occurs after the tashahhud, building is permissible because the only remaining obligation is exiting the prayer by his own choice. The commentary clarifies that if the imam does not appoint a substitute and leaves the mosque, the congregation's prayer is invalid unless there are connected rows outside. For the follower, the ruling depends on whether his imam (the substitute) has finished the prayer: if he has finished, the follower may complete where he made wudu or return; if not, he must return and complete behind the substitute. The passage then addresses exceptional cases: madness, fainting, and wet dream. Madness and fainting invalidate wudu by consensus, so they necessitate the same options. A wet dream during prayer is possible if one sleeps in a manner that does not invalidate wudu (e.g., sleep in ruku' or sujud). The commentary emphasizes that if a barrier (e.g., a river) exists between the prayer spot and wudu spot, the person is obligated to return to ensure the validity of following the imam; otherwise, he may choose.

Key Terms
الاستئناف (al-isti'naf): Starting the prayer anew after performing wudu, i.e., cutting the current prayer and re-starting.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): The act of the imam appointing a substitute (khalifah) to lead the remaining part of the prayer.
البناء (al-bina'): Continuing the same prayer after wudu from the point where hadath occurred, without starting over.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who is led by the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must the imam do if he experiences hadath during prayer and there is a barrier (e.g., a river) between his place of prayer and his place of wudu?
A) He must return to the original place and complete the prayer there.
B) He must complete the prayer where he performed wudu and cannot return.
C) He is given a choice between returning and completing there.
D) He must appoint a substitute and cannot return himself.

Key Takeaway
When hadath occurs during prayer, the Hanafi school offers a choice between building and starting anew, with isti'naf being the preferred option, and the imam may appoint a substitute via gesture.

Salah — Prayer

Nullifiers of Wudu in Salah and the Imam's Return
Ruling with proof on nullifiers and imam's return

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the events that nullify wudu during salah and explain the Hanafi ruling on the imam's return and the effect of leaving the mosque.

Core Idea
Loud laughter (qahqaha) and intentional hadath nullify wudu; the mosque is a single place allowing continuation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains which events break wudu during prayer and how the imam or follower should proceed if such an event occurs. It also clarifies a key Hanafi principle: the mosque is considered one place, so leaving it is required for invalidation of prayer after a nullifying event.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is being discussed (e.g., prayer, imam's appointment) and the overall hukm when a nullifier occurs: the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated after renewing wudu.
2
List the nullifiers of wudu in salah
Go through each event: madness, fainting, wet dream (during sleep that does not nullify wudu), qahqaha (loud laughter), intentional hadath, large najasah, and head wound causing blood flow. Note the distinction between nullifying wudu and merely invalidating prayer.
Smiling and ordinary laughter do not nullify wudu.
3
Apply the ruling on the imam's return
Understand the scenario: the original imam appoints a deputy (khalifa) who leads the rest of the prayer. If the deputy finishes, the original imam completes elsewhere or returns; if not, he returns and prays behind the deputy. The follower is likewise.
Return is obligatory if there is a barrier preventing following; otherwise optional.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on leaving the mosque
The text states that if one thinks he nullified wudu and leaves the mosque, the prayer is invalid. If he stays, he completes. Imam Muhammad's analogy (qiyas) would require restart regardless, but the relied-upon position (istihsan) treats the mosque as one place.
The thamarah al-khilaf: staying in the mosque saves the prayer; leaving invalidates.

[٤] قوله: أو شج؛ بصيغة المجهول، عطف على الأفعال السابقة، ويحتمل أن يكون بفتح الشين المعجمة، وتشديد الجيم، مصدراً معطوفاً على البول، والحاصل أن يصيبه حجرٌ أو مدرّ أو غير ذلك برأسه فيشجّه ويجرحه، فيسيل من شجته الدم، فينتقض وضوؤه به ولازمه بطلان صلاته، [0] قوله: فخرج من المسجد؛ قيَّد به؛ لأنه لو لم يخرج من المسجد لا تبطل، بل يُصلّي ما بقي؛ لأن المسجد مع تباين أطرافه بمنزلة مكان واحد، بدليل صحة الاقتداء، وعدم تكرر وجوب سجدة التلاوة، والقياس الاستئناف مطلقاً، رواية عن محمد له؛ لوجود الانحراف عن القبلة والمشي. If his imam finishes [the prayer], otherwise he returns, and similarly the follower. And if he becomes mad, or faints, or has a wet dream, and if he wishes, he returns. (If his imam finishes): connected to his statement: 'And he completes there or returns.' The pronoun in 'his imam' refers back to the first imam, and 'his imam' is the one he appointed as deputy, for the deputy is an imam for the first imam and for the people. (Otherwise he returns): i.e., if his imam—the deputy—has not finished, the [original] imam returns and completes behind his deputy. [2] (And similarly the follower): i.e., if his imam finishes, he completes there or returns; if not, he returns. (And if he becomes mad, or faints, or has a wet dream): i.e., he sleeps in his prayer such that his wudu is not nullified by it, then has a wet dream. [4] [1] His statement: 'he returns': i.e., obligatorily, if between the place of prayer and the place of his wudu there is nothing that prevents the validity of following [the imam], such as a road, a river, and the like. If there is, he chooses between returning and completing in that place. [2] His statement: 'he returns': necessarily, if between him and his imam there is something that prevents the validity of following; if not, he does not return, and he follows from there. This is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah and al-Binayah. (3) His statement: 'and if he becomes mad': with dammah on the jim and shaddah on the nun; i.e., madness occurs to him during his prayer. It is well-known that madness nullifies wudu. [4] His statement: 'or faints': in the passive form, not using the common form; i.e., fainting occurs to him, which is in Persian: بيهوشي, and it nullifies wudu. [0] His statement: 'i.e., he sleeps': Since one might think that a wet dream only occurs during sleep, so how can it occur during his prayer? He pointed to refuting this and explained its scenario: that he sleeps in his prayer and has a wet dream in it. Then, since one might think that sleep itself nullifies wudu, so his wudu would be nullified without the wet dream, he restricted it by his statement: 'such that his wudu is not nullified by it', i.e., he sleeps in his prayer in a state where his wudu is not nullified by it, like sleeping in ruku' and sujud, then has a wet dream in it. If the author had said 'or he has an emission' it would have been better, because 'wet dream' is usually used for emission during a dream (with dammah on the lam) which is sleep, while 'emission' is more general, and it can occur in prayer by thinking and emitting, or looking at a woman and emitting. In that case, there is no need for the burden of depicting [sleep]. [1] His statement: 'or he laughs loudly': i.e., he laughs in prayer with qahqaha laughter, which is that which can be heard by those near him. It is well-known that qahqaha in prayer is among the nullifiers of wudu. Indeed, [ordinary] laughter does not nullify it but invalidates the prayer, and smiling neither nullifies nor invalidates. We have elaborated on this in the treatise 'al-Hashashah fi Naqd al-Wudu' bi al-Qahqaha'. (2) His statement: 'or he intentionally passes wind': i.e., he deliberately passes wind in his prayer. If he did not intend it but it preceded him, its ruling has already been mentioned: he performs wudu and builds. [3] His statement: 'or a large amount of urine befalls him': what is meant is an amount that legally prevents the validity of prayer. Urine is mentioned as an example. The intention is that a najasah befalls him in an amount not excused by the Law, so his garment or body becomes impure. [4] His statement: 'or he is wounded': in the passive form, conjoined to the preceding verbs. It is also possible that it is with fatha on the shin and shaddah on the jim, as a masdar conjoined to 'urine'. The summary is that a stone, clod, or something else strikes his head and wounds it, making blood flow from the wound. Thus his wudu is nullified by it, and consequently his prayer is invalidated. [0] His statement: 'so he leaves the mosque': he restricted it by this because if he does not leave the mosque, it is not invalidated; rather, he prays what remains. Because the mosque, despite the differences of its sides, is considered a single place, evidenced by the validity of following, and the non-repetition of the obligation of the prostration of recitation. The analogy [qiyas] would be starting over absolutely, according to a narration from Muhammad, due to the deviation from the qiblah and walking. (1) 'al-Hashashah fi Naqd al-Wudu' bi al-Qahqaha' (p. 95). And it is.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah regarding events that nullify wudu during salah. The author explains the rulings concerning the original imam and follower when the imam finishes or does not finish his prayer; then discusses specific nullifiers. The imam who appointed a deputy returns and completes behind the deputy if the deputy has not finished. The follower similarly either completes or returns. For madness, fainting, and wet dream: these nullify wudu, thus invalidate the prayer. The commentator clarifies that wet dream occurs during sleep that does not itself nullify wudu (e.g., during ruku' or sujud). He notes that if the author had said 'or emits' it would be more comprehensive. Then he discusses loud laughter (qahqaha): it nullifies wudu and invalidates prayer; ordinary laughter only invalidates but does not nullify wudu; smiling does nothing. Intentional passing of wind (hadath 'amdan) nullifies wudu; if unintentional, one performs wudu and builds upon the prayer. A large amount of impurity (e.g., urine) that is beyond the excused amount nullifies wudu. Being wounded (shajj) with blood flow nullifies wudu and invalidates prayer. Finally, if one thinks he nullified wudu and leaves the mosque, his prayer is invalidated only if he leaves the mosque; if he remains in the mosque, he continues. The commentator notes an analogy (qiyas) from Imam Muhammad that leaving would necessitate starting over due to deviation from qiblah and walking, but the relied-upon position is that the mosque is a single place, so leaving is necessary for invalidation.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter in prayer that can be heard by those near him; it nullifies wudu and invalidates prayer.
أحدث عمداً (ahdatha amdan): To intentionally pass wind during prayer; this nullifies wudu and invalidates the prayer.
احتلم (ihtalam): To have a wet dream (i.e., nocturnal emission) during sleep while in prayer; it nullifies wudu.
شج (shajj): A wound to the head that causes blood to flow; it nullifies wudu and invalidates prayer.
خليفة (khalifa): Deputy imam appointed by the original imam to lead the rest of the prayer when the original imam becomes unable to continue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person intentionally passes wind (ahdatha amdan) during salah?
A) The prayer becomes invalid but wudu remains valid.
B) Both wudu and prayer are nullified.
C) Only wudu is nullified; the prayer continues after performing wudu.
D) The prayer is invalid only if he leaves the mosque.

Key Takeaway
Loud laughter (qahqaha) and intentional hadath nullify wudu and invalidate prayer; the mosque is treated as one place, so leaving it is required for invalidation after a nullifying event.

Salah — Prayer

Events That Invalidate or Allow Building in Prayer
Commentary on invalidating events in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each event that occurs in prayer (qahqaha, hadath, najis, shajj, mistaken impurity) and apply the conditions under which building (bina') is permitted.

Core Idea
Building is only allowed for unintentional, external, non-rare hadath; all else invalidates the prayer.

In prayer, various events can interrupt the act. The Hanafi school distinguishes between events that nullify wudu and those that just invalidate the prayer, and between intentional and unintentional acts. A key feature is the concept of building (bina'), where one may continue after re-purifying in certain cases. This lesson examines each event and the rationale behind the permission to build.

Guided Path
1
Define each event and its immediate ruling
List the events mentioned: qahqaha (loud laughter), intentional/unintentional hadath, large najis, shajj (head wound), and mistaken impurity leading to leaving the mosque. For each, note whether it nullifies wudu, invalidates prayer, or both.
The passage also covers rare events like insanity and ihtilam, which do not permit building.
2
Distinguish intentional vs unintentional hadath for building
The hadith permits building only for unintentional hadath (that which occurs without choice). Intentional hadath before tashahhud invalidates the prayer entirely.
After tashahhud, intentional hadath allows completion due to exiting by own action.
3
Analyze the effect of place change on building
If mistakenly thinking you are impure and you leave the mosque or exceed the rows in the desert, the prayer is invalidated because the place changed. Building is not allowed because intention of rectification only avails when the place remains the same.
The entire mosque is considered one place; leaving it breaks the continuity.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad narrates that building is allowed even after leaving the mosque if the person intended rectification, but the commentary sides with the view that place change invalidates tahrima.
The preferred (mufta bihi) position is that building is not allowed after changing place.
5
Understand the rationale for limiting building to specific events
The hadith that permits building is contrary to qiyas and therefore confined to its occasion: events that exit the body, are external, and are not rare. Events like insanity, qahqaha, ihtilam, or intentional hadath do not meet these criteria.
Events that nullify ghusl (like ihtilam) are not included because the hadith only mentions wudu nullifiers.

Or he laughed loudly, or intentionally broke wudu, or a large amount of urine hit him, or he was wounded and blood flowed, or he thought he broke wudu and left the mosque—the first [ruling] is more appropriate because ihtilam is usually used for ejaculation during a dream—with a damma—which is sleep, and ejaculation is more general than it, and it can occur in prayer by him reflecting so he ejaculates, or looking at a woman so he ejaculates, so there is no need for effort in illustration. [1] His statement: 'or he laughed loudly'; meaning he laughed in prayer the laughter of qahqaha, which is what makes his voice heard by those near him, and it is known that qahqaha in prayer is one of the nullifiers of wudu; indeed, ordinary laughter does not nullify wudu but invalidates the prayer, and smiling neither nullifies nor invalidates. [2] His statement: 'or intentionally broke wudu'; meaning he passed wind in his prayer deliberately; if he did not intend it but it preceded him, its ruling has already passed that he should perform wudu and build upon his prayer. [3] His statement: 'or a large amount of urine hit him'; what is meant is an amount that prevents the validity of prayer according to the Shari'a, and the mention of urine is by way of example; the intent is that an impurity hits him in an amount that is not excused in the Shari'a, so his garment or body becomes impure. [4] His statement: 'or he was wounded'; in the passive form, conjoined to the previous verbs; it can be with a fatha on the shin and shadda on the jim, as a masdar conjoined to urine; the result is that a stone, clod of earth, or something else hits his head, wounding and cutting him, so blood flows from his wound, thereby nullifying his wudu and his prayer. [5] His statement: 'so he left the mosque'; he restricted it because if he did not leave the mosque, it would not be invalidated, but he would pray what remains; because the mosque, despite the difference of its parts, is like a single place, as evidenced by the validity of following the imam and the non-repetition of the obligation of the prostration of recitation; and the analogy is to restart absolutely, [but there is] a narration from Muhammad in favor of building due to the existence of turning from the qibla and walking. Or he exceeded the rows outside, then his purity became apparent, [the prayer] is invalidated. And the reason for the distinction according to us is that he turned away with the intention of rectification, not rejection; do you not see that if he intended what he thought was his prayer, the walking and turning would not harm him? So the intention of rectification is attached to its reality as long as the place does not differ; because its difference without an excuse invalidates the tahrima, so building is not sound. Thus in Al-Hidayah and Al-Binaya. [1] His statement: 'or he exceeded the rows'; conjoined to his statement 'left'; meaning that the criterion is his leaving the mosque if he is in it, and exceeding the rows if he is outside it; for the place of rows in the desert has the same ruling as the mosque. And all of this is if he turns to his back; if he walks forward, the limit is the sutra, and if there is no sutra, then the extent of the rows behind him; and the criterion for a person praying alone in this chapter is the place of his prostration from every side. Thus in Al-Hidayah. [2] His statement: 'then his purity became apparent'; with a damma on the important ta; meaning his being pure became apparent, and he knew that his assumption was wrong. [3] His statement: 'is invalidated'; the apodosis of his statement: 'and if he becomes insane... etc.'; meaning the prayer is invalidated by the occurrence of these events in it, so restarting is obligatory. As for the case of insanity, unconsciousness, and qahqaha; because although they are nullifiers of wudu, they are not events exiting the body, and also they are rare; and the hadith that rules the permissibility of building, which came contrary to analogy, was only reported concerning events exiting the body that are not rare, so it is confined to its occasion, and what is not of its kind is not attached to it. As for the case of ihtilam and the like, because it is an event that nullifies ghusl, and the hadith only permitted building for nullifiers of wudu, so what is not like it is not attached to it. As for the case of intentional hadath, because building is only permitted in the case of it preceding [him] without choice, and intentionality contradicts it; thus intentional hadath invalidates the prayer if it occurs before tashahhud, and he completes it if it occurs after it, due to the existence of exiting by his own action.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining a list of events that occur during prayer and their legal effects according to the Hanafi school. The author first clarifies that the word 'ihtilam' is usually used for ejaculation during sleep, but it can also occur in wakefulness through reflection or looking, so there is no need for artificial examples. He then defines qahqaha as laughter that is heard by those nearby, stating it nullifies wudu, whereas ordinary laughter only invalidates prayer and smiling does nothing. Intentional passing of wind nullifies the prayer and requires restart, but if unintentional, one may perform wudu and build upon the prayer. Being hit by a large amount of impurity (exemplified by urine) that is not excused nullifies the prayer. A wound that causes blood to flow also nullifies wudu and the prayer. If someone mistakenly thinks he has broken wudu and leaves the mosque, his prayer is invalidated because leaving the mosque constitutes a change of place; however, if he stays inside, he can complete the prayer because the entire mosque is considered one place. The commentary notes that analogy would require restarting, but there is a narration from Imam Muhammad allowing building due to the presence of turning and walking. For someone outside the mosque (in the desert), exceeding the rows has the same effect as leaving the mosque. If he then discovers he was actually pure, the prayer is invalidated because his departure was based on a mistaken assumption; but if he intended to rectify the prayer, the prayer is not invalidated as long as the place does not differ. Finally, the commentary explains why building is not allowed for insanity, unconsciousness, qahqaha, ihtilam, and intentional hadath: the hadith on building only applies to unintentional, external events that are not rare; these events either are not external, are rare, nullify ghusl rather than wudu, or are intentional.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter that is heard by those nearby, which nullifies wudu and invalidates prayer.
حدث (hadath): Breaking of wudu, either by passing wind or other causes. The passage distinguishes intentional (nullifies prayer without building) and unintentional (allows building).
بناء (bina): Continuing the prayer from where one left off after performing wudu, without restarting.
شج (shajj): A wound on the head that causes blood to flow, nullifying wudu and prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, what is the ruling if someone intentionally breaks wudu during prayer before the tashahhud?
A) He may perform wudu and build upon his prayer.
B) The prayer is invalidated and he must restart.
C) He can complete the prayer without wudu.
D) He performs wudu and then repeats the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The permission to build in prayer is strictly limited: it applies only to unintentional, external, and common events that nullify wudu, not to intentional acts, rare events, or those that nullify ghusl.

The Invalidity of Building After Mistaken Impurity
Commentary on building when purity becomes apparent after leaving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that leaving the prayer space based on a mistaken assumption of impurity invalidates the prayer and prohibits building.

Core Idea
A mistaken assumption of impurity does not excuse leaving the prayer space; building is only for genuine events.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah explains a nuanced scenario in the prayer: a person mistakenly believes he has become impure (e.g., passed wind) and leaves the mosque or crosses in front of the rows to rectify. Upon discovering he was pure, the question arises: can he continue his prayer from where he left off? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the prayer is invalid because the change of place without a valid excuse breaks the taḥrīmah. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and distinguishes between valid and invalid cases of building.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving the mosque or crossing rows in prayer due to a mistaken belief of impurity. The ruling is that the prayer becomes invalid (bāṭil) and must be restarted; building is not allowed.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith reported by Ibn Mājah and al-Dāraquṭnī: 'Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed in his prayer, let him leave, perform wuḍū', and build upon his prayer as long as he has not spoken.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith permits building only for specific events (vomiting, nosebleed, etc.). The Hanafi school interprets this as a limited exception (khārij 'an al-qiyās) and does not extend it to other situations.
The exception is restricted to genuine, non-rare events exiting the body.
4
Note the exception and its limits
Building is only allowed when the person left for a genuine, non-rare event (like vomiting) and did not change place significantly. Leaving due to a mistaken assumption or for a rare event (like insanity) does not qualify.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Other schools may allow building more broadly. The Hanafi position is based on strict adherence to the text and qiyās.

Source Text

ولو لم يخرج أو لم يتجاوز بَنَى : اعلم أن هذه الحوادث حوادث نادرة، فلم تكن في معنى ما وَرَدَ به النَّص ، وهو قوله : «مَنْ قَاءَ ، أَوْ رَعَفَ فِي صلَاتِهِ، فَلْيَنْصَرِفُ، وَلِيَتَوَضًا وَلِيَبْنِ عَلَى صَلَاتِهِ مَا لَمْ يَتَكَلَّم». وأما في صورة إصابة البول ؛ فلأنَّ البناء إنّما ورد في سبق الأحداث، فلا تلحق به صور الأنجاس. وأما في صورة سيلان الدم من الشجّة ؛ فلكونه نادر الوجود، فلا يلحق بمورد الحديث. وأما في صورة الخروج من المسجدِ والتجاوز من الصفوف، فلكونه من النوادر، مع كون مورد الحديث حقيقة الحدث، فلا تلحق به صورة الظن الذي تبين خطؤه. وبالجملة : فهذه العوارض لما لم تكن من جنس ما ورد به الحديث المجوّز للبناء لم يكن أن تلحق به الحوق النظير بالنظير، ولا أن تقاس عليه ؛ لعدم جواز القياس على الخارج عن القياس ، فلذلك حكم ببطلان الصلاة بها، وعدم جواز البناء بها على ما هو القياس في الجميع. And the aspect of the difference according to us is that he turned away with the intention of correction, not rejection. Do you not see that if he had considered what he thought about his prayer, it would not harm him, and walking and turning do not harm him? So the intention of correction is attached to its reality as long as the place does not differ. For if the place differs without an excuse, it invalidates the taḥrīmah, so building is not valid. Thus in 'al-Hidāyah' and 'al-Bināyah'. [1] His statement: 'Or he crossed the rows' is conjunct to his statement: 'left', meaning that what is considered is his leaving the mosque if he is in it, and crossing the rows if he is outside. For the place of the rows in the desert has the ruling of the mosque. All this if he turned to his back. If he walked forward, the limit is the sutrah, and if there is none, then the extent of the rows behind him. And what is considered for the individual in this chapter is the place of his prostration from every side. Thus in 'al-Hidāyah'. [2] His statement: 'Then his purity became apparent' with ḍammah on the ṭā' al-muhmalah; i.e., it became evident that he was pure, and he knew that his assumption was wrong. [3] His statement: 'it is invalidated' is the result of his statement: 'And if he becomes insane... etc.' meaning that the prayer is invalidated by the occurrence of these accidents in it, so re-starting is required. As for the case of insanity, fainting, and roaring laughter: because even though they are nullifiers of wuḍū', they are not events exiting from the body, and also they are rare. And the hadith that rules permissibility of building, which came contrary to qiyās, only came for events exiting from the body that are not rare, so it is restricted to its context, and what is not of its kind is not attached to it. As for the case of wet dream and the like: because it is an event that nullifies ghusl, and the hadith only came for building with nullifiers of wuḍū' only, so what is not its like is not attached. As for the case of intentional event: because building is only permitted in the case of unintentional precedence, and intentionality contradicts it. So an intentional event invalidates the prayer if it occurs before tashahhud, and completes it if it occurs after, due to the existence of exit by his own action, as the author will mention. And if he did not leave or did not cross, he builds. Know that these accidents are rare events, so they are not in the meaning of what the text came with, which is his statement: 'Whoever vomits or has a nosebleed in his prayer, let him leave, perform wuḍū', and build upon his prayer as long as he has not spoken.' And as for the case of urine striking: because building only came for precedence of events, so images of najāsāt are not attached. And as for the case of blood flowing from a head wound: because it is rare, so it is not attached to the scope of the hadith. And as for the case of leaving the mosque and crossing the rows: because it is of the rare, while the scope of the hadith is actual event, so the case of an assumption that turns out to be wrong is not attached. In summary: these accidents, since they are not of the kind that the hadith permitting building came for, they cannot be attached to it by analogy of like to like, nor be qiyās upon it, due to the impermissibility of qiyās upon what is outside qiyās. Therefore, it is ruled that the prayer is invalidated by them, and it is not permissible to build upon them, according to what is the qiyās in all. [1] His statement: 'which is his statement' and it was narrated by Ibn Mājah via Ismā'īl ibn 'Ayyāsh from Ibn Jurayj from Ibn Abī Mulaykah from 'Ā'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever vomits, or has a nosebleed, or emits madhy in his prayer...' the hadith. And it was narrated by al-Dāraquṭnī with the wording: 'Whoever is struck by vomiting, nosebleed, qalas, or madhy, let him leave, perform wuḍū', and build upon his prayer while he does not speak.'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharḥ) on a ruling from the matn of al-Wiqāyah. It addresses the situation where a person praying (musallī) mistakenly believes he has become impure (e.g., he thinks he passed wind) and therefore leaves the mosque or crosses in front of the rows (in an open area) to go to the toilet. However, after doing so, he realizes that he was actually still pure (his assumption was wrong). The ruling is that his prayer is invalid (bāṭil); he cannot simply 'build' upon it (i.e., continue from where he left off). The commentary explains the reasoning: the person turned away from the prayer with the intention of correcting a perceived impurity, not with the intention of abandoning the prayer. Normally, such an intention would allow building (binā') even if there is some movement, as long as the place of prayer does not change. But in this case, the place does change—either by leaving the mosque or by moving beyond the rows—without a valid excuse (since he was actually pure). This change of place without an excuse breaks the fundamental prohibition of worldly actions (taḥrīmah), which is the essence of starting the prayer. Therefore, building is not allowed. The commentary then goes through several related cases to distinguish where building is allowed and where it is not. It categorizes accidents into those that are like the hadith case (non-rare body events like vomiting/nosebleed) and those that are different (rare events, intentional events, mental states, contamination by najāsah). The key principle is that the hadith permitting building is an exception to qiyās (analogy); therefore, it cannot be extended beyond its specific scope. The hadith itself is cited at the end, showing the proof for the original permission to build for genuine events like vomiting/nosebleed. Thus, this passage clarifies the boundary of the exception.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbīr of the prayer, which makes worldly actions forbidden (ḥarām) and establishes the state of iḥrām for the prayer.
البناء (al-binā'): Continuing the prayer from where one left off after performing an ablution or removing an impurity, without restarting.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): A legal impurity requiring wuḍū' (minor ḥadath) or ghusl (major ḥadath), such as passing wind, urine, or sexual defilement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person leaves the mosque during prayer because he thinks he has broken his wuḍū', but then realizes he was actually pure, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) He may continue his prayer from where he left off (building).
B) His prayer is invalid and he must restart.
C) He must perform wuḍū' and then continue.
D) His prayer is valid as long as he returned quickly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not allow building when a person leaves the prayer space based on a mistaken assumption of impurity; the prayer must be restarted.

The Ruling on Building (Bina') After Hadath in Salah
Commentary on the hadith permitting building and its limitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building after hadath in salah and identify which specific events permit it.

Core Idea
Building after hadath is a text-based concession limited to few events; analogy cannot extend it.

The Hanafi school holds that if a person experiences a sudden, rare event like vomiting or a nosebleed during prayer, he may leave, perform wudu, and continue from where he left off. This concession, known as bina', is an exception to the general rule that any hadath invalidates the prayer. In this passage, the commentator explains the limitation of this ruling and why it cannot be applied to other impurities or interruptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its explicit events
Locate the hadith quoted in the text: 'Whoever vomits or gets a nosebleed in his prayer, let him leave, perform wudu, and continue.' Note that vomiting and nosebleed are specifically mentioned; other versions add qals (regurgitation) and madhy.
The hadith is classed as authentic by some scholars, and the Hanafi school accepts its mursal version.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on building
Based on the hadith, building is permissible (mubah) only for the specific events listed. The ruling is a concession (rukhsah) for rare occurrences.
The imperative 'فليتوضأ' indicates permissibility, not obligation.
3
Analyze why other events are excluded
The text discusses four excluded cases: urine contamination (najasah), blood from a head wound, exiting the mosque/passing rows, and a suspicion that turns out wrong. Each is excluded because it is not of the same type as the hadith events or is too rare in a different sense.
The commentator emphasizes that these are not 'in the meaning' of the text.
4
Understand the principle: no analogy on exceptions
The author states that the ruling in the hadith is an exception to general qiyas (which would require restarting prayer after hadath). Exceptions cannot be extended by analogy because they are 'outside analogy.' Therefore, building is not allowed for any unmentioned event.
This is a key usul al-fiqh point: kharaja 'an al-qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو لم يخرج ، أو لم يتجاوز بَنَى : اعلم أن هذه الحوادث حوادث نادرة، فلم تكن في معنى ما وَرَدَ به النَّص ، وهو قوله : «مَنْ قَاءَ ، أَوْ رَعَفَ فِي صلَاتِهِ، فَلْيَنْصَرِفُ، وَلِيَتَوَضًا وَلِيَبْنِ عَلَى صَلَاتِهِ مَا لَمْ يَتَكَلَّم». وأما في صورة إصابة البول ؛ فلأنَّ البناء إنّما ورد في سبق الأحداث، فلا تلحق به صور الأنجاس. الحديث. وأما في صورة سيلان الدم من الشجّة ؛ فلكونه نادر الوجود، فلا يلحق بمورد وأما في صورة الخروج من المسجدِ والتجاوز من الصفوف، فلكونه من النوادر، مع كون مورد الحديث حقيقة الحدث، فلا تلحق به صورة الظن الذي تبين خطؤه. وبالجملة : فهذه العوارض لما لم تكن من جنس ما ورد به الحديث المجوّز للبناء لم يكن أن تلحق به الحوق النظير بالنظير، ولا أن تقاس عليه ؛ لعدم جواز القياس على الخارج عن القياس ، فلذلك حكم ببطلان الصلاة بها، وعدم جواز البناء بها على ما هو القياس في الجميع. [ 1 ] قوله : وهو قوله لله و أخرجه ابن ماجة من طريق اسماعيل بن عياش عن ابن جريح عن ابن أبي مليكة عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «مَن قاء أو رعف(۱) أو أمذى في صلاته.... الحديث، وأخرجه الدارقطني بلفظ : «من أصابه قيء أو رعاف أو قلس أو مذي (۳) فلينصرف فليتوضأ، وليين على صلاته وهو في ذلك لا يتكلم». (۱) الرعاف : وهو خروج الدم من الأنف. ينظر : «المصباح المنير»(ص۲۳۰)، وغيره. (۲) القلس : ما خرج من بطنه طعام أو شراب إلى الفم وسواء ألقاه أو أعاده إلى بطنه إذا كان ملء الفم أو دونه فإذا غلب فهو قيء. ينظر : ((المصباح» (ص ٥۱۳ ) ، و (طلبة الطلبة» (ص۸)، وغيرها. (۳) في سنن ابن ماجه (۱) : (۳۸۵) ، واللفظ له، وسنن الدارقطني (۱) : ١٥٥)، قال الزيلعي في نصب الراية» (۱ : ۳۸) : حديث عائشة رضي الله عنه صحيح. - وعن أبي الدرداء له: إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قاء فأفطر فتوضأ فلقيت ثوبان في مسجد دمشق فذكرت ذلك له فقال : صدق أنا صببت له الدفع في سنن الترمذي (۱) : ١٤٣)، وقال: قد جود حسين المعلم هذا الحديث وحديث حسين أصح شيء في هذا الباب وروى معمر هذا الحديث وفي كلا السندين ضعف، نعم ؛ صحح حفاظ الحديث طريقاً له مرسلة، وهو ما ورده عن ابن جريح عن أبيه عن النبي له مثله مرسلاً ، ذكره الدارقطني في «كتاب العلل»، نقله ابن حجر في «تلخيص الحبير»). (1) (۲) والمرسل حجة عندنا ، وينجبر الضعفُ بالآثار الواردة في ذلك، فإن ابن أبي شَيْبَةَ روى البناء وجوازه عن علي وأبي بكر الصديق وسلمان وابن عمر وابن مسعود ، ومن المعلوم أن آثار الصحابة له فيما يخالف القياس ملحقة بالمرفوع، على ما هو مقرّر في كتب أصول الحديث. وفي موطأ مالك» أيضا آثار في ذلك، وقد بسطت الكلام في المسألة في حواشي على موطأ مالك برواية محمّد المسمّاة بـ«التعليق الممجد».
And if he did not exit, or did not exceed, he builds (bina). Know that these events are rare events, so they are not in the meaning of what the text came with, which is his statement: 'Whoever vomits or gets a nosebleed in his prayer, let him leave, perform wudu, and continue his prayer as long as he does not speak.' As for the case of urine contamination: because building was only reported for preceding of events, so the cases of impurities are not attached to it. And as for the case of blood flowing from a head wound: because it is rare in existence, so it is not attached to the source. And as for the case of exiting the mosque and passing beyond rows: because it is from the rare occurrences, while the source of the hadith is the essence of hadath, so the case of suspicion that turns out to be wrong is not attached to it. In summary: these accidents, since they are not of the type that the hadith permitting building came about, it is not possible to attach them to the analogous with the analogous, nor to analogize them, due to the lack of permissibility of analogy on that which is outside analogy. Therefore, it was ruled that the prayer is invalid due to them, and the impermissibility of building due to them, as is the analogy in all. [1] His statement: and his statement—Allah—and Ibn Majah narrated it from Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash from Ibn Jurayj from Ibn Abi Mulayka from 'A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever vomits or gets a nosebleed or has madhy in his prayer...' the hadith, and al-Daraqutni narrated it with the wording: 'Whoever is afflicted with vomiting, nosebleed, qals, or madhy, let him leave, perform wudu, and continue his prayer while not speaking.' (1) Nosebleed: the exit of blood from the nose. See al-Misbah al-Munir (p. 230) and others. (2) Qals: what exits from his stomach of food or drink to the mouth, whether he spits it out or returns it to his stomach, if it fills the mouth or less, and if it overcomes then it is vomiting. See al-Misbah (p. 513) and Talbat al-Talaba (p. 8), etc. (3) In Sunan Ibn Majah (1:385), the wording is his, and Sunan al-Daraqutni (1:155), al-Zayla'i said in Nasb al-Rayah (1:38): The hadith of 'A'isha is authentic. And from Abu al-Darda: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) vomited, so he broke his fast, performed wudu, then I met Thawban in the mosque of Damascus and mentioned that to him, and he said: He spoke the truth; I poured for him the water in Sunan al-Tirmidhi (1:143), and he said: Husayn al-Mu'allim transmitted this hadith well, and the hadith of Husayn is the most authentic thing in this chapter, and Ma'mar narrated this hadith. The chains are both weak; however, the hadith scholars authenticated a way of it as mursal, which is what was reported from Ibn Jurayj from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him) similar to it as mursal, mentioned by al-Daraqutni in Kitab al-'Ilal, transmitted by Ibn Hajar in Talkhis al-Habir. (1) (2) And the mursal is a proof with us, and the weakness is compensated by the reports that have come in that regard. Ibn Abi Shayba narrated building and its permissibility from 'Ali, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Salman, Ibn 'Umar, and Ibn Mas'ud. And it is known that the effects of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) in that which opposes analogy are attached to the marfu', as established in books of hadith principles. In the Muwatta of Malik there are also reports in that regard, and I have expanded the discussion on the issue in my commentary on the Muwatta of Malik in the narration of Muhammad, named al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn line regarding the ruling of building (bina') after a hadath during salah. The author begins by stating that the ruling is based on a specific hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which permits the one who vomits or has a nosebleed to leave, perform wudu, and continue the prayer. He then explains that this concession is limited to the events mentioned in the hadith; other types of impurities or events (like urine contamination, blood from a wound, leaving the mosque, or passing through rows) are not included because they are either not of the same type or are too rare. The author argues that these exceptional cases cannot be extended by analogy (qiyas) because the original ruling itself is an exception to general principles of prayer invalidity. He then discusses the authenticity of the hadith, noting its multiple chains and the acceptance of mursal hadith in the Hanafi school. He also cites the practice of several Companions to support the ruling. The passage concludes that the prayer is invalid in other cases and building is not allowed.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu and requires renewal for prayer.
بناء (bina'): Continuing the prayer from where one left off after performing wudu, without restarting.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here, the author states qiyas cannot be applied because the ruling is an exception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, in which of the following cases is building (bina') after hadath permitted?
A) Intentional hadath after tashahhud
B) Vomiting during prayer
C) Touching impurities (najasah) during prayer
D) Sneezing during prayer

Key Takeaway
Building after hadath is a text-specific concession limited to a few rare events and cannot be extended by analogy.

Intentional Hadath After Tashahhud: Completeness vs. Sinfulness
Commentary on the matn line about intentional hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intentional hadath after tashahhud and explain the distinction between the prayer being technically complete and the act being sinful.

Core Idea
A prayer can be technically complete yet the act of ending it by breaking wudu is a major sin.

This passage addresses a controversial Hanafi ruling: if someone intentionally breaks wudu after the final tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete. Critics have long derided this as permitting sin. The commentator clarifies that 'complete' means the obligation is discharged, but the act is haram and the prayer should be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being discussed? What is the ruling (hukm) stated?
The act is intentional hadath after tashahhud; the ruling is that the prayer is 'tammat' (complete).
2
Analyze the meaning of 'tamam'
Examine how the commentator defines 'tamam' in this context. Is it perfection or something else?
It means bara'at al-dhimmah (discharge of responsibility), not perfection.
3
Understand the consequence
What are the consequences of this act? Is there a sin? Is repetition required?
The act is haram, the prayer is makruh tahrimi, and repetition (i'ada) is preferred because the wajib salam is left.
4
Refute the common misunderstanding
How does the commentator respond to critics who say the Hanafis permit the act?
He strongly denies this, stating that the Hanafis hold salam as wajib and leaving it is sinful.
5
Contrast with involuntary hadath
What is the ruling for involuntary hadath according to the hadith from Ibn 'Umar? How does this contrast?
Involuntary hadath allows return and building upon the prayer; intentional hadath does not, highlighting the difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله: تمت ; معنى التمام هاهنا براءة الذمة من الصلاة بأداء الأركان والفرائض، ولا مناص من لزومِ الإثم ولزوم الكراهة التحريمية، ووجوب الإعادة ؛ لترك لفظ : : «السلام» الواجب الموضوع شرعاً لإتمام الصلاة، وقد طال طعن السفهاء على الحنفية في مسألة الحدث، واستقبحوا الحكم بتمام الصلاة بالحدث عمدا، فمنهم من ظنّ أنّهم يجوزون مثل هذا الفعل، والخروج، وليس كذلك. فإنّ الخروج بالسلام عندنا واجب ، وتركُ الواجب عندنا مكروه تحريماً، بـل حرام، فلا مناص عن لزوم الإثم، ومنهم من ظنّ أنّ معنى التمام هـو البراءة من النقصان، وليس كذلك، فأي نقصان وشناعة أشدّ من ترك السلام الذي وضع للتحليل، واختيار الحدثِ عمداً للفراغ من الصلاة التي هي أفضل العبادات وأعزّها، وليس مرادهم بالتمام إلا ما ذكرنا. وعن ابن عمر قال : «إذا رعف الرجل في الصلاة، أو ذرعه القيء، أو وجد مذياً فإنه ينصرف ويتوضأ ثم يرجع فيتم ما بقي على ما مضى ما لم يتكلم» في «مصنف عبد الرزاق» (۲ : ۳۳۹) ، وإسناده صحيح كما في إعلاء السنن»(١ : ١١٤)، وغيره. (۱) تلخيص الحبير» (١) : ٢٧٤). (۲) التعليق الممجد (۱ : ٥٢٣ - .(٥٢٤
[1] His statement: 'completed' (tammat). The meaning of completion here is the freedom of the responsibility from the prayer through performing the pillars and obligatory acts, and there is no escape from the necessity of sin and the necessity of karahah tahrimiyyah, and the obligation of repetition (i'ada) because of leaving the word 'salam' which is obligatory, placed by law to complete the prayer. The insults of the foolish against the Hanafis in the issue of hadath have long continued, and they deemed the ruling of completing the prayer by intentional hadath as reprehensible. Some of them thought that they permit such an act and exiting (from prayer), but it is not so. Indeed, exiting by salam is obligatory with us, and leaving the obligatory with us is makruh tahrimi, rather haram, so there is no escape from the necessity of sin. Some of them thought that the meaning of completion is freedom from deficiency, but it is not so. What deficiency and atrocity is greater than leaving the salam which is placed for tahlil, and choosing intentional hadath to finish the prayer which is the best of worship and the most noble? Their intention with completion is only what we mentioned. And from Ibn 'Umar, he said: 'If a man has a nosebleed in prayer, or is overcome by vomiting, or finds madhy, then he leaves, performs wudu, then returns and completes what remains of what has passed, as long as he does not speak.' [In] Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq (2:339), and its chain is authentic as in I'la' al-Sunan (1:114), and others. (1) Talkhis al-Habir (1:274). (2) Al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad (1:523-524).
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn line 'ولو أحدث عمداً بعد التشهد... تمت' (And if he intentionally hadath after tashahhud... it is complete). The author clarifies the Hanafi position: the prayer is considered complete (tammat) meaning the responsibility (dhimmah) is discharged because the essential acts (arkan and fara'id) have been performed. However, deliberately breaking wudu is a sin (haram) because it involves leaving the obligatory salam (salutation) without necessity. The act is considered makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The author strongly refutes critics who misinterpret this ruling as allowing sin or claiming the prayer is free from deficiency. He explains that 'completion' here does not mean the prayer is perfect or free from deficiency, but that the obligation is fulfilled technically while the person is guilty of a serious transgression. The author then quotes a hadith from Ibn 'Umar about involuntary hadath, providing an example of the normal ruling for building after involuntary hadath, contrasting with the intentional hadath case discussed here.

Key Terms
تمام (tamam): Completion; here meaning the obligation of prayer is discharged (bara'at al-dhimmah) even though the prayer is not perfect.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an act that is close to haram, requiring repentance and compensation (here, repetition of prayer).
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of the prayer due to omission of a wajib element (here, the salam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, what is the ruling on a person who intentionally breaks wudu after tashahhud?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be fully repeated.
B) The prayer is complete and no repetition is needed.
C) The prayer is complete but the act is sinful and the prayer should ideally be repeated.
D) The prayer is valid without any sin because tashahhud substitutes for salam.

Key Takeaway
Intentional hadath after tashahhud completes the prayer technically but is a major sin; the prayer should be repeated.

Twelve Invalidators After Tashahhud According to Abu Hanifa
Listing and explaining twelve cases where prayer is invalidated after tashahhud according to Abu Hanifa, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve cases that invalidate prayer after tashahhud according to Abu Hanifa, explain the underlying principle (al-khuruj bi-sun'ihi as fard), and compare the position of the Sahibayn, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The Hanafi dispute: does prayer after tashahhud need an intentional exit? Abu Hanifa says yes, the Sahibayn say no.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to the prayer when certain events occur after the tashahhud but before the salam? Imam Abu Hanifa lists twelve cases that invalidate the prayer, while his companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the prayer is already complete and remains valid. Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of Hanafi usul and the role of intention in exiting the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
Read the initial objection and response. Determine what Abu Hanifa considers a fard (obligatory) in exiting the prayer.
The key term is 'al-khuruj bi-sun'ihi' (exiting by one's own action).
2
Review the objection and response
Understand the objection that exiting may involve sin (like lying or hadath) and cannot be fard. Note the response that the fard is the exit itself, not the action causing it.
Analogy with hudud and qisas: the caused (execution) is different from the cause (murder).
3
Enumerate the twelve cases
Go through each of the twelve cases listed and see how they relate to the principle: in each case, the exit is not by the person's own voluntary action due to an external factor.
The cases are: seeing water, removing khuff, expiry of wiping duration, unlettered person learning, naked person getting clothing, ability to perform pillars, remembering missed prayer, qari stepping forward unlettered, sunrise in Fajr, entry of Asr in Jumu'ah, removal of excuse, falling of splint.
4
Compare with the Sahibayn's position
Note that the Sahibayn do not consider exiting by one's own action as fard; for them, the prayer is complete after tashahhud. Therefore, none of these cases invalidate the prayer.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates that the relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn. Confirm from al-Hidayah and later works.
The practice of fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بأن ألقاه أحد عليه، فتبطل صلاته ؛ لرفع العجز. وقدرة المومئ على الأركان، وتذكر فائتة وتقديم القارئ أمياً، وطلوع ذكاء في الفجر، ودخول وقت العصرِ في الجمعة، وزوالُ عُذرِ المعذور، وسقوط الجبيرة عن برء.
